Selling Measured Goods Before Re-Measurement: The Seller's Measurement in the Buyer's Presence
Ruling on prohibition and exception for buyer's presence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling measured goods before re-measurement, identify when the seller's measurement suffices, and apply the condition of the buyer's presence.

Core Idea
The seller's measurement suffices if done in the buyer's presence, but not otherwise.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq clarifies a key rule in sales transactions: when someone buys goods by volume or weight, may they sell them before re-measuring them? The general position is that re-measurement is required, but there is an important exception when the measurement occurs in the buyer's presence. We will examine the proof, the exception, and a branch case to ensure precise application.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
From Zahir al-Riwāyah, if a person buys goods by measure (mukāyalah), takes possession, and then sells them by guess (mujāzafah) before re-measuring, the sale is not permissible due to the risk of mixing ownership.
This is the default ruling; the buyer must re-measure after possession before selling.
2
Identify the exception
If the seller measured the goods in the buyer's presence, that measurement suffices for both, and the buyer may sell without re-measuring. This is the correct view (al-ṣaḥīḥ).
The hadith requiring two measures is fulfilled by the seller's measure and the buyer's witnessing.
3
Understand the condition of 'presence'
The buyer's presence does not require sight of the actual weighing; knowing the weight and the scale suffices, as in the baker example from al-Quniyah.
Presence (ḥaḍrah) is general: the buyer may see or not, as long as the measurement is transparent.
4
Apply the branch case
If food is measured in a man's presence, he buys it in the same session, then sells it by measure before re-measuring it himself, the sale is invalid because he was not in possession (he never measured for himself). This holds whether he measured for his seller or not.
The ruling distinguishes possession by one's own measurement vs. seller's measurement.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Ibn Samā'ah in the Nawadir permits selling before re-measurement even without the buyer's presence, but the relied-upon position (muftā bihī) is the majority view.
The ikhtilaf is within the madhhab; the mufta bihi is the stricter view requiring presence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشترى مكايلة ثم باع مجازفة قبل الكيل وبعد القبض في ظاهر الرواية لا يجوز لا حتمال اختلاط ملك البائع بملك بائعه. وفي نوادر ابن سماعة : يجوز وإنما يحتاج إلى كيل البائع إذا كان البائع اشتراه مكايلة وظاهر كلام المصنف يدل على أن كيل البائع لا يكفي عن كيل المشتري وهو محمول على ما إذا كاله البائع قبل البيع مطلقاً أو بعده في غيبة المشتري، أما إذا كاله في حضرته فإنه يغني عن كيله وهو الصحيح لأن المبيع صار معلوماً بكيل واحد وتحقق معنى التسليم، ومحمل الحديث اجتماع الصفقتين على ما تبين في السلم إن شاء الله تعالى؛ كذا في الهداية. ومن هنا ينشأ فرع وهو ما لو كيل طعام بحضرة رجل ثم اشتراه في المجلس ثم باعه مكايلة قبل أن يكتاله بعد شرائه لا يجوز هذا البيع سواء اكتاله للمشتري منه أو لا، لأنه لما لم يكتل بعد شرائه هو لم يكن قابضاً فبيعه بيع ما لم يقبض؛ كذا في فتح القدير قوله : (أما إذا كان في حضرته فإنه يغني عن كيله أي عن كيل المشتري قيماً يظهر، وعليه فصورة المسألة اشتراه مكايلة وكاله لنفسه ثم باعه كذلك وكاله بحضرة المشتري منه أغنى ذلك المشتري عن كيله . ويحتمل عود الضمير إلى البائع وصورته اشتراه مكايلة ولم يكله لنفسه حتى باعه من آخر وكاله بحضرة المشتري منه فإنه يغني عن كيله أي كيل البائع، ويدل على هذا التعليل بقوله لأن المبيع صار معلوماً بكيل واحد وهذا هو المتبادر من كلام الهداية فراجعه لكن ينافيه قوله ومن هنا ينشأ فرع الخ» فإن قوله سواء اكتاله للمشتري منه أو لا يدل على أن كيله للمشتري منه قبل كيله لنفسه لا يغني عن كيله اللهم إلا أن يحمل على أن كيله للمشتري منه وقع في غيبة ذلك المشتري أو يقال إن اللام في قوله للمشتري منه زائدة من تحريف النساخ وأصلها همزة الوصل. وأقول : المراد بالحضرة أعم من أن يراه أو لا. قال في القنية بعد ما رقم (مح) : يشتري من الخباز خبزاً كذا منا فيزنه وكفة سنجات ميزانه في دربنده فلا يراه المشتري أو من البائع كذا مناً فيزنه في حانوته ثم يخرجه إليه موزوناً لا يجب عليه إعادة الوزن، وكذا إذا لم يعرف عدد سنجاته. قال رضي الله تعال عنه : فعرف بهذا أنه إذا عرف المشتري وزن السنجات ورآها أن يكتفي بذلك خلاف ما دل عليه ظاهر نهي النبي عليه السلام عن بيع الطعام حتى يجري فيه صاعان صاع البائع وصاع المشتري اهـ.
He bought by measure, then sold by guess before measurement and after possession; in the apparent narration it is not permissible due to the possibility of mixing the seller's property with his seller's property. In the Nawadir of Ibn Samā'ah: it is permissible. And the seller's measurement is only needed if the seller bought it by measure. The apparent speech of the author indicates that the seller's measurement does not suffice for the buyer's measurement, and it is interpreted as when the seller measured it before the sale absolutely or after it in the buyer's absence. But if he measured it in his presence, it suffices for his measurement, and that is the correct view because the sold item became known by one measurement and the meaning of delivery is realized. The interpretation of the hadith is the joining of the two transactions as explained in salam, God willing. This is from al-Hidāyah. From here arises a branch: if food is measured in the presence of a man, then he buys it in the session, then sells it by measure before measuring it after his purchase, this sale is not permissible, whether he measured it for his own seller or not, because since he did not measure it after his purchase, he was not a possessor, so his sale is selling what he has not taken possession; this is from Fatḥ al-Qadīr. Then the commentary explains the phrase: 'As for when it was in his presence, it suffices for his measurement' i.e., the buyer's measurement, apparently. So the scenario: he bought it by measure and measured it for himself, then sold it likewise, and the measurement was in the presence of his buyer, that suffices the buyer from measuring. But it is possible the pronoun refers to the seller, and the scenario: he bought by measure and did not measure it for himself until he sold it to another, and he measured it in the presence of that buyer, then it suffices for his measurement i.e., the seller's measurement. This is supported by his saying 'the sold item became known by one measurement'. This is what is understood from al-Hidāyah, but it contradicts his saying 'From here arises a branch' etc. For his saying 'whether he measured it for his seller or not' indicates that his measuring for his seller before measuring for himself does not suffice for his measurement unless it is interpreted that his measuring for his seller occurred in the buyer's absence, or it is said that the lam in 'for his seller' is extra from the copyists' distortion and its original is the hamzah of connection. I say: presence is general whether he sees him or not. It is stated in al-Quniyah: he buys from the baker bread of so many manns, he weighs it with the weights of his scale in his shop, the buyer does not see it, or from the seller so many manns, he weighs it in his shop then brings it out to him weighed, he is not required to re-weigh. Similarly if he does not know the number of his weights. The author (may God be pleased with him) said: thus it is known that if the buyer knows the weight of the weights and sees them, it suffices, contrary to the apparent meaning of the Prophet's prohibition of selling food until two measures are used: the seller's measure and the buyer's measure.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq regarding the permissibility of selling measured goods before re-measurement after possession. The text opens with the general rule from Zahir al-Riwāyah: it is not permissible for someone who bought goods by measure to sell them by guess before re-measuring them after taking possession, because of the risk that the buyer's property might be mixed with the seller's property. However, a rare transmission from Ibn Samā'ah permits it. The author then clarifies the condition for the seller's measurement to suffice for the buyer: if the seller measured the goods before the sale or after it in the buyer's absence, it does not suffice. But if the seller measured in the buyer's presence, it does suffice, and this is the correct position because the goods are then known by a single measurement. This is based on the hadith about measuring twice. The text then presents a branch case: if food is measured in a man's presence, he buys it in the same session, then sells it by measure before re-measuring it himself, the sale is invalid because he was not yet in possession. This applies whether he measured it for his own seller or not. The commentary then examines the phrase 'in his presence', concluding that it covers cases where the buyer does not see the measurement physically but knows the weights. The example from al-Quniyah of buying bread from a baker confirms that if the buyer knows the weights and sees them, he need not re-weigh. This guards against the misunderstanding that the buyer must always physically perform the measurement himself.

Key Terms
مكايلة (mukāyalah): A sale measured by volume (kayl).
مجازفة (mujāzafah): A sale by guess or approximation without precise measurement.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books.
حضرة (ḥaḍrah): Presence; the buyer's awareness of the measurement, even if not seeing the actual weighing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer purchases a sack of flour by weight. The seller weighs it in the buyer's presence. The buyer then sells the flour by weight to a third party without re-weighing. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, this sale is:
A) Invalid, because the buyer must re-weigh after possession.
B) Valid, because the seller's measurement in the buyer's presence suffices.
C) Valid only if the buyer also weighs it in front of his own buyer.
D) Invalid, because it is a sale by guess.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires re-measurement after possession unless the seller measured in the buyer's presence.

Disposal of Price Before Receipt: Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling with proof: permissibility of disposing price before receipt, with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of the price before receipt, explain the legal reasoning, and identify the exceptions of sarf and salam.

Core Idea
Disposal of the price before receipt is valid because ownership of a debt is absolute; exceptions are sarf and salam.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling: that the seller may dispose of the price (a debt) before physically receiving it. The ruling is based on the principle that ownership of a debt is absolute, and there is no risk of rescission due to destruction. However, exceptions exist for sarf (exchange of gold/silver) and salam (forward sale), where the price is treated like the sold item itself. We will explore the proof and the scope of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is disposal (tasarruf) of the price (thaman) before physical receipt (qabd). The Hanafi ruling is permissibility (ja'iz), meaning it is valid and allowed.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy): ownership of the debt is established at the time of contract, and there is no gharar (uncertainty) because the price is not a specific object that can be destroyed. Hence, disposal is a function of ownership.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is that the price is a dayn (debt), and ownership of a debt is absolute in Hanafi fiqh. Since the debt is not subject to physical destruction, there is no prejudice in disposing of it before receipt.
4
Note the istithna' (exception)
The ruling does not apply to sarf (exchange of gold/silver) and salam (forward sale). In these transactions, the price is considered like the sold item (mabi'), and disposal before possession is prohibited by a clear hadith.
5
Evaluate the scope
The ruling covers all types of debts: mahr (dower), rental, liability for damages, etc. However, giving ownership of the debt to a third party (other than the debtor) is not permissible, as it would be transferring debt without the debtor's consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصح التصرف في الثمن قبل قبضه لقيام المطلق وهو الملك وليس فيه غرر الانفساخ بالهلاك لعدم تعينها بالتعيين بخلاف المبيع؛ كذا في الهداية وظاهره أنه مخصوص بما لا يتعين والحكم أعم منه ولذا قال في فتح القدير : سواء كان مما يتعين أو لا سوى بدل الصرف والسلم لأن للمقبوض حكم عين المبيع سيأتي متناً وإنما هو استظهار لوجه الحلقة بالمنصوص عليه في الحديث كما هو أظهر الروايتين. في السلم والاستبدال بالمبيع قبل القبض لا يجوز، وكذا في الصرف وأيده السمع إلى آخره . وأطلق التصرف قبل قبضه لقيام المطلق فشمل البيع والهبة والأجارة والوصية وتمليكه ممن عليه بعوض وغير عوض إلا تمليكه من غير من هو عليه فإنه لا يجوز. وأشار المؤلف بالثمن إلى كل دين فيجوز التصرف في الديون كلها قبل قبضها من المهر والإجارة وضمان المتلفات سوى الصرف والسلم ما قدمناه وأما التصرف في الموروث والموصى به قبل القبض فقدمنا جوازه
His saying: (And disposal of the price before its receipt is valid) because the absolute (i.e., ownership) exists, and there is no risk of rescission due to destruction because it is not specified by identification unlike the sold item; this is from al-Hidāyah. Its apparent meaning is that it is specific to what is not specified, but the ruling is more general than that, so it is said in Fatḥ al-Qadīr: whether it is of the type that is specified or not, except for the countervalue in ṣarf and salam, because what is received has the ruling of the very sold item as will come in the matn. It is only a consideration of the aspect of the link according to the text of the hadith, as it is the more apparent of the two narrations. In salam and substitution of the sold item before receipt: it is not permitted, and similarly in ṣarf, and this is supported by the hearing etc. He made disposal before his receipt absolute because of the existence of the absolute, so it includes sale, gift, lease, bequest, and giving ownership to the one on whom it is due with or without compensation, except giving ownership to someone other than the one on whom it is due: that is not permissible. The author indicated by 'price' every debt: so disposal of all debts before their receipt is permissible, including dower, lease, liability for damages, except ṣarf and salam as we have mentioned. As for disposal of inherited property and bequeathed property before receipt, we have already stated its permissibility.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This ruling addresses the validity of disposing of the price (thaman) before physically receiving it. The key principle is that the price is a debt (dayn) in the seller's liability, and the seller's ownership over that debt is established at the time of contract. Since the price is not a specific identified object, there is no risk of the contract being rescinded due to destruction of the price object (unlike the sold item which is specific and can be destroyed). Therefore, the seller can sell, gift, lease, bequeath, or assign the debt to the debtor before taking possession. However, this does not apply to two cases: ṣarf (exchange of gold/silver) and salam (forward sale), because in those, what is received has the ruling of the sold item itself, and disposal before possession is prohibited by clear hadith. The text clarifies that the ruling is general for all debts, whether specified or not, and includes various types of debts like dower (mahr), rental, and damages. The exception is giving ownership of the debt to someone other than the debtor; that is not allowed because it would be a transfer of debt without the debtor's consent. The passage also notes that disposal of inherited or bequeathed property before possession is permissible, as previously established.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale, which is a debt on the buyer until paid.
قبض (qabd): Physical or constructive taking possession of the subject matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following transactions is disposal of the price before receipt NOT permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sale of a house on credit
B) Exchange of gold for silver (sarf)
C) Lease of a property for monthly rent
D) Sale of wheat on credit

Key Takeaway
Disposal of the price before receipt is generally valid in Hanafi fiqh because ownership of a debt is absolute, with the sole exceptions of sarf and salam.

Increase and Reduction in Price: Do They Attach to the Contract?
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on price modification attachment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on increase and reduction in price, explain Zafar's objection, and apply the ruling in the six consequential cases.

Core Idea
Increase and reduction in price change the contract's description, not its essence, so they attach.

When parties agree to increase or reduce the price after a sale contract, is this a modification of the existing contract or a new gift? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, holds that it attaches, while Zafar considers it a separate gift. This dispute has practical implications for pre-emption, cost-based sales, and third-party claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the dispute
State that according to the Hanafi school (the position of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn), an increase (ziyādah) or reduction (ḥaṭṭ) in the price after the contract is valid and attaches to the original contract. Note that Zafar disagrees, considering them separate gifts.
Attachment means the modification is considered part of the original contract.
2
Understand Zafar's objection
Zafar argues that the increase cannot be part of the price because the price is already fixed for the item; any change would alter the exchange ratio, so it must be a new gift. Similarly, reduction removes part of the price, which is impossible since the entire price corresponds to the entire item.
Zafar's view is a minority opinion within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that increase/reduction only change the contractual description (profit, loss, or cost), not the essence of the contract. Since the parties have authority to rescind the contract entirely, they have even greater authority to modify its description. This is analogous to stipulating or canceling an option after the contract.
The analogy to options (khiyār) is a key proof.
4
Distinguish total reduction
Note that a total reduction (ḥaṭṭ al-kull) – i.e., giving the item for free – is a change of essence, not description, so it does not attach but is a new gift. The text restricts 'reduction from it' to partial reduction.
Total reduction is treated as an independent gift (ṣilah).
5
Apply the ruling in consequential cases
The attachment has practical effects in six issues: (1) tawliyah (sale at cost) – valid on total with increase; (2) murābaḥah (profit sale) – valid on remainder after reduction; (3) shuf'ah (pre-emption) – pre-emptor takes at reduced price, not forced to pay increase; (4) istihqāq (third party claim) – buyer recovers full price from seller; (5) ḥabs al-mabī' (right to hold item) – seller may hold until increase paid; (6) a sixth incomplete in text.
These consequences stem from the price modification being part of the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والزيادة فيه أي صحت الزيادة في الثمن قوله: (والحط منه) أي من الثمن ويلتحقان بأصل العقد عندنا، وعند زفر لا يلتحقان وإنما يصحان على اعتبار ابتداء الصلة لأنه لا يمكن تصحيح الزيادة ثمناً لأنه ملکه عوض ملكه فلا يلتحق بأصل العقد، يصير وكذا الحط لأن كل الثمن صار مقابلاً بكل المبيع فلا يمكن اخراجه فصار براً مبتدأ. ولنا أنهما بالحط والزيادة يغير إن العقد من وصف مشروع إلى وصف مشروع وهو كونه رابحاً أو خساراً أو عدلاً ولهما ولاية الرفع فأولى أن يكون لهما ولاية التغيير فصار كما إذا اسقطا الخيار أو شرطاه بعد العقد، وإذا صح يلتحق بالعقد لأن وصف الشيء يقوم به لا بنفسه بخلاف حط الكل لأنه تبديل لأصله لا تغيير لوصفه ولذا قيد بقوله «منه» لإخراج حط الكل، وفائدة الالتحاق تظهر في مسائل : الأولى التولية الثانية المرابحة فيجوز على الكل في الزيادة وعلى الباقي بعد المحطوط الثالثة الشفعة حتى يأخذ الشفيع بما بقي في الحط، وإنما كان له أن يأخذ بدون الزيادة لما فيها من إبطال حقه الثابت فلا يملكانه. الرابعة في الاستحقاق حتى يتعلق الاستحقاق بالجميع فيرجع المشتري على البائع بالكل ولو أجاز المستحق البيع أخذ الكل. الخامسة في حبس المبيع فله حبسه حتى يقبض الزيادة. السادسة الخ» قوله : (وكذا الحط) أي لا يلتحق بأصل العقد وقوله فلا يمكن إخراجه أي إخراج كل الثمن عن المقابلة بكل المبيع؛ كذا في الحواشي السعدية . قوله : (لأن وصف الشيء يقوم به يعني أن الزيادة في الثمن والحط منه وصف له فتلتحق
His saying: (And the increase in it) i.e., the increase in the price is valid. His saying: (and the reduction from it) i.e., from the price, and they attach to the original contract according to us (Hanafis). According to Zafar, they do not attach; rather they are valid on the basis of initiating a gift, because it is not possible to validate the increase as part of the price since it is his property in exchange for his property, so it does not attach to the original contract. Similarly for reduction, because all of the price is in exchange for all of the sold item, so it cannot be removed, so it becomes an independent gift. Our argument: they (buyer and seller) change the contract from one lawful description to another lawful description, i.e., profit, loss, or parity, and they have the authority to rescind, so they have even more authority to change; it becomes like canceling an option or stipulating it after the contract. If valid, it attaches to the contract because the description of a thing is inherent in it, not independent, unlike total reduction because that is a change of the essence, not a change of description. Hence he restricted by saying 'from it' to exclude total reduction. The benefit of attachment appears in several issues: first: tawliyah (sale at cost); second: murabahah (sale with stated profit) – it is valid on the whole for increase, and on the remainder after reduction; third: shuf'ah (pre-emption) – the pre-emptor takes at the reduced price, and he is not forced to take with the increase because that would nullify his established right, so they (the original parties) cannot impose it; fourth: istihqaq (third party claim) – the entire sale is subject to claim, so the buyer recovers the full price from the seller, and if the claimant validates the sale, he takes the entire thing; fifth: habs al-mabi' (right to hold the sold item) – he may hold it until he receives the increase; sixth: ... (incomplete). His saying: (and similarly the reduction) i.e., it does not attach to the original contract. And his saying 'so it cannot be removed' i.e., removing all of the price from being in exchange for all of the sold item; this is from al-Hawāshī al-Sa'diyyah. His saying: (because the description of a thing is inherent in it) means that the increase in the price and reduction from it are descriptions of it, so they attach.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi position that an increase (ziyādah) or reduction (ḥaṭṭ) in the price after the contract is valid and attaches to the original contract, meaning it is considered a modification of the contract rather than a separate independent transaction. Against this, Zafar holds that increase and reduction cannot attach; they are separate acts of gift (ṣilah) because the price is already fixed for the item, and altering it would change the exchange ratio. The Hanafi argument is that increase and reduction only change the description of the contract (e.g., from profit to loss or to cost), not its essence. Since the parties have the right to cancel the contract entirely, they have even more right to modify it. This is analogous to stipulating or canceling an option after the contract. The attachment has practical consequences in six cases: (1) Tawliyah (sale at cost) – valid with increase on total, etc.; (2) Murābaḥah (sale with stated profit) – valid on the remaining after reduction; (3) Shuf'ah (pre-emption) – the pre-emptor takes at the reduced price, not forced to pay increase; (4) Istihqāq (third party claim) – the buyer recovers the full price from seller if the item is taken; (5) Ḥabs al-mabī' – seller can hold the item until he receives the increase; (6) (not fully given). A total reduction (ḥaṭṭ al-kull) is different because it changes the essence; it does not attach but is a new gift. The text ends with the principle that increase/reduction are descriptions of the price and therefore attach to the contract.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyādah): An increase in the price agreed upon in the contract.
حط (ḥaṭṭ): A reduction in the price from the agreed amount.
التولية (al-tawliyah): A sale where the buyer takes the item at the seller's cost price, often after purchase.
الشُّفعة (al-shuf'ah): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase the sold property at the price agreed by the buyer.
الاستحقاق (al-istihqāq): A third party's claim of ownership over the sold item, requiring return to the claimant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a buyer and seller agree to increase the price after the contract is concluded, what is the legal status?
A) The increase is void because the contract is already concluded.
B) The increase is valid as a new independent gift.
C) The increase is valid and attaches to the original contract.
D) The increase requires a new contract to be valid.

Key Takeaway
Increase and reduction in price (partial) attach to the original contract as descriptions, not as separate gifts, affecting pre-emption, cost sales, claims, and holding rights.

Increase and Decrease in Price Attach to the Contract
Ruling that increase and decrease in price are valid and modify the contract's description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on post-contract price modifications, explain the qiyas-based proof, and distinguish the attachment theory from Zufar's independent-gift view.

Core Idea
An increase or decrease in price after a sale attaches to the contract, modifying its description without creating a new contract.

In Hanafi law, parties may voluntarily agree to raise or lower the price after a sale is concluded. A fundamental question arises: does this create a new contract or merely modify the existing one? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling that such changes 'attach' to the original contract, the internal disagreement with Imam Zufar, and the practical implications for transactions like tawliyah, murabahah, and shuf'ah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the core legal position: both increase (ziyada) and decrease (hatt) in price are valid and attach to the original contract, altering its description (e.g., from profit to break-even).
This is the majority view within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand Zufar's objection
Imam Zufar argues that the increase cannot be part of the price because the buyer owns the sold item as a substitute for the price; similarly, the decrease cannot be extracted from the price already allocated. Therefore, both must be independent gifts (sila or ibra).
Zufar's view is a legitimate intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (qiyas)
The Hanafi response uses analogy: just as the parties have the authority to annul the contract (raf'), they have authority to change its description (wasf). Changing the price description is like adding or cancelling an option (khiyar) after the contract. This proves attachment.
The analogy is based on the parties' contractual autonomy.
4
Derive the thamarah (practical effect)
If it attaches, the new price governs the entire transaction for purposes like tawliyah, murabahah, shuf'ah, istihqaq, and the seller's right to withhold the sold item. If separate, the original price remains and the increase/decrease is a separate gift.
The practical difference is key in legal application.
5
Apply to consequences
Work through the five issues listed: (1) Tawliyah – the new price is passed on; (2) Murabahah – profit calculated on adjusted price; (3) Shuf'ah – preemptor takes at decreased price but cannot be forced to pay increase; (4) Istihqaq – entire transaction subject to claim at new price; (5) Hubs (right to withhold) – seller may withhold until increase is paid.
These illustrate why the attachment theory matters in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والزيادة فيه) أي صحت الزيادة في الثمن قوله: (والحط منه) أي من الثمن ويلتحقان بأصل العقد عندنا، وعند زفر لا يلتحقان وإنما يصحان على اعتبار ابتداء الصلة لأنه لا يمكن تصحيح الزيادة ثمناً لأنه ملکه عوض ملكه فلا يلتحق بأصل العقد، يصير وكذا الحط لأن كل الثمن صار مقابلاً بكل المبيع فلا يمكن اخراجه فصار براً مبتدأ. ولنا أنهما بالحط والزيادة يغير إن العقد من وصف مشروع إلى وصف مشروع وهو كونه رابحاً أو خساراً أو عدلاً ولهما ولاية الرفع فأولى أن يكون لهما ولاية التغيير فصار كما إذا اسقطا الخيار أو شرطاه بعد العقد، وإذا صح يلتحق بالعقد لأن وصف الشيء يقوم به لا بنفسه بخلاف حط الكل لأنه تبديل لأصله لا تغيير لوصفه ولذا قيد بقوله «منه» لإخراج حط الكل، وفائدة الالتحاق تظهر في مسائل : الأولى التولية الثانية المرابحة فيجوز على الكل في الزيادة وعلى الباقي بعد المحطوط الثالثة الشفعة حتى يأخذ الشفيع بما بقي في الحط، وإنما كان له أن يأخذ بدون الزيادة لما فيها من إبطال حقه الثابت فلا يملكانه. الرابعة في الاستحقاق حتى يتعلق الاستحقاق بالجميع فيرجع المشتري على البائع بالكل ولو أجاز المستحق البيع أخذ الكل. الخامسة في حبس المبيع فله حبسه حتى يقبض الزيادة. السادسة
His saying: (And the increase in it) means the increase in the price is valid. His saying: (And the decrease from it) means from the price, and both attach to the original contract according to us. According to Zufar, they do not attach; rather they are valid on the basis of initiating a gift, because it is not possible to validate the increase as a price since he owned a substitute for his ownership, so it does not attach to the original contract; likewise the decrease because all of the price has become a substitute for all of the sold item, so it cannot be extracted, so it becomes a pure gift. Our proof: by decrease and increase they change the contract from one lawful description to another lawful description, namely being profitable or loss-making or break-even, and they have the authority to annul, so it is more appropriate that they have the authority to change, so it becomes like when they cancel an option or stipulate it after the contract. And if it is valid, it attaches to the contract because the description of a thing is attached to it, not to itself; unlike the decrease of the whole because that is a change of its essence, not a change of its description. Therefore he restricted his saying 'from it' to exclude the decrease of the whole. The benefit of attachment appears in issues: First: Tawliyah; Second: Murabahah; so it is valid on the total for the increase and on the remainder after the decreased part; Third: Shuf'ah; so the preemptor takes at what remains after the decrease; he may take without the increase because that would nullify his right, so they do not own it; Fourth: Istihqaq; so the entitlement relates to the whole, so the buyer returns to the seller for the whole, and if the entitled person validates the sale, he takes the whole; Fifth: Hubs of the sold item; so he has the right to withhold it until he receives the increase; Sixth: ...
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling that an increase (ziyadah) or decrease (hatt) in the price after the contract is valid and attaches to the original contract according to the Hanafi school. The commentator presents the position of Zufar (a Hanafi imam) who disagrees, holding that such additions are only valid as independent gifts (ibrā' or ṣilah) because the price has already been fixed as a substitute for the sold item. The Hanafi response uses analogy (qiyās): just as the parties have the authority to annul the contract (raf'), they have authority to change its description (waṣf). Since increase or decrease changes the description (profitable, loss-making, or break-even) without altering the essence of the contract, it attaches to the original contract, similar to adding or canceling an option (khiyār) after the contract. The commentator then lists five practical consequences (fawā'id) of this attachment: (1) in tawliyah, the new price is taken as a whole with the increase or after the decrease; (2) in murābaḥah, the profit is calculated on the adjusted price; (3) in shuf'ah, the preemptor may take at the decreased price but cannot be forced to pay the increase; (4) in the case of istiḥqāq (a third party proving ownership), the entire transaction is subject to the claim; (5) the seller may withhold the sold item until the increase is paid. The sixth issue is not elaborated here.

Key Terms
الزيادة (az-ziyāda): An increase in the price after the contract, voluntarily agreed by the parties.
الحط (al-ḥaṭṭ): A decrease or reduction in the price after the contract.
التولية (at-tawliya): A sale at the original cost price without profit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It creates a new separate contract.
B) It is invalid because the price is fixed.
C) It attaches to the original contract as a change in its description.
D) It is treated as a gift that does not affect the sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, post-contract price modifications attach to the original contract and modify its description, affecting subsequent transactions like tawliyah, murabahah, and shuf'ah.

Increase and Decrease in Price: The Condition of the Sold Item's Existence
Intra-Hanafi dispute on increase/decrease and condition of remaining sold item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on increase and decrease in price after sale, and apply the condition that the sold item must remain in existence for an increase to be valid.

Core Idea
Increase attaches only if the sold item remains a proper object of exchange; decrease is easier and may stand as a gift.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute about post-contract adjustments to the price. Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ on whether an increase or decrease (hatt) is valid as part of the original sale or must be treated as a separate transaction. The central point is the condition of baqā' al-mabī' — the sold item must still exist in a form suitable for exchange for the increase to attach to the contract. We will walk through the three positions, the evidence, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions
List what Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad each say about increase and decrease in price. Note that Abu Yusuf rejects both as attachments but does not invalidate the sale; Muhammad agrees on increase but permits decrease as an independent gift; Abu Hanifa holds both can attach under conditions.
This ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school itself.
2
Understand the condition for increase
From al-Hidayah and al-Khulasa, the increase is valid only if the sold item remains (baqā') in a state that can be exchanged. If the item is completely destroyed (e.g., natural death), increase is invalid. Partial transformation (slaughter, rent, pawn) may still allow increase because the form and some benefits remain.
The opposite condition applies to decrease – it is easier because it reduces the price without demanding a new substitute.
3
Apply the conditions to cases
Work through the examples given: a sheep that dies vs. one that is slaughtered; a slave-girl who is freed, given tadbir, etc. Determine which actions preserve the item as a proper object of exchange and which do not.
The key distinction: complete destruction vs. transformation where name, form, and some benefits survive.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text indicates that the condition of existence from al-Hidayah is relied upon, and the fatwa follows the permissive view of Abu Hanifa for transformations. Thus, increase can attach as long as the item is not completely annihilated.
This is a case where the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is balanced with practical flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Regarding the invalidity of sarf by decrease or increase due to riba, as if they contracted it as unequal from the beginning. Abu Yusuf prevented the validity of increase and decrease in it and did not invalidate the sale; Muhammad agreed with him regarding increase and permitted decrease as an initiated gift; in al-Khulasa. The author did not mention a condition for the validity of increase in the price, and a condition for it is mentioned in al-Hidayah: the sold item must remain (in existence) for it to be valid after its destruction? No, in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) because the sold item did not remain in a state that makes exchange valid for it, and the thing is established then attributed, unlike decrease because it is possible to extract the substitute for what corresponds to it, so it attaches to the original contract by attribution. Contrary to increase in the sold item itself, for it is permissible after its destruction because it is established in exchange for the price which is existent; thus in al-Khulasa. And in al-Khulasa also: Its condition in the price from the buyers is the existence of the sold item and its being a proper object of exchange in the buyer's right actually. If it was a slave-girl and he freed her, or made a tadbir, or had a child with her, or made kitaba, or sold her to another after taking possession, then increased in the price, it is not valid. What is mentioned in the book is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) saying, and they narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is valid even if he rented her or pawned her, or bought a sheep and slaughtered it, then increased in the price, it is valid; contrary to if the sheep died then he increased in the price, it is not valid because it did not remain a proper object for sale, unlike the first where the name, form, and some benefits exist. The summary of this is in the book Nazm al-Zandustani: He said: ...

Commentary
This section presents the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding increase and decrease in price, and the condition that the sold item must remain in existence for an increase to be valid. Abu Yusuf held that both increase and decrease are invalid as attachments but do not nullify the sale; Muhammad agreed on increase allowing decrease only as a separate gift (hiba). The text then details the condition for increase: the sold item must survive in a state that can be exchanged for the price. If the item is completely destroyed (e.g., sheep dies), increase is invalid because the item is no longer a proper object of exchange. However, if the item is transformed (e.g., slaughtered sheep, or rented/pawed slave-girl), increase is valid because some form or benefit remains. The commentator refers to al-Hidayah and al-Khulasa for these conditions and notes a transmission from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that allows increase in certain transformations.

الزيادة (al-ziyāda): Increase in price after the contract.

Increase and Reduction in Sarf: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on increase/reduction in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on increase and reduction in sarf and explain the talil behind each view.

Core Idea
Increase and reduction in sarf cause fasad; reduction can be valid as a gift.

This passage addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding post-contractual modifications in currency exchange (sarf). While both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree that increase (ziyada) after the contract renders the transaction fasid (corrupt), they diverge on reduction (hatt). Understanding their analogical reasoning (talil) is key to grasping the Hanafi approach to riba and contractual amendments.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the legal act: post-contract increase or reduction in a sarf (ribawi) sale. What is the default ruling?
The text treats any increase or reduction as if the contract was originally made with that disparity.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Yusuf holds that both increase and reduction are invalid but the sale remains valid (fasid, not batil). Muhammad agrees on increase but permits reduction as an independent gift (hiba mubtada'a).
Both are Hanafi imams; the dispute is intra-madhhab.
3
Analyze the talil (legal reasoning)
Increase is traced back (yuthabbu thumma yastanidu) to the original contract, requiring the sold item to still exist for compensation. Reduction can attach (yalhaqu) because it is possible to extract a substitute for the portion reduced.
The condition for increase validity is that the sold item remains; otherwise, increase is invalid.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Under Abu Yusuf, both modifications cause fasad but the contract is not void. Under Muhammad, reduction is a separate valid gift, so the sale remains sound.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, if reduction occurs, Abu Yusuf considers the contract fasid, Muhammad considers it valid with a gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on increase (ziyada) and reduction (hatt) in the price or commodity in a currency exchange (sarf) contract. The key issue is that any increase or reduction is treated as if the contract was originally made with that disparity, leading to riba. Abu Yusuf (رحمه الله) holds that both increase and reduction are invalid but do not nullify the entire sale. Muhammad (رحمه الله) agrees on increase but considers reduction as a separate gift (hiba), thus valid. The author notes that a condition for the validity of increase in price is that the sold item must still exist; otherwise, it is invalid in the apparent narration. The reasoning is that increase establishes a new right that is traced back to the original contract, while reduction can attach because it is possible to extract a substitute for the portion reduced.

Key Terms

حط (hatt): Reduction; reducing the price or commodity after the contract.
زيادة (ziyada): Increase; adding to the price or commodity after the contract.

Increase in Price: Condition and the 11/12 List
Ruling on condition for increase in price with detailed examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid increase in price and classify actions as preserving or destroying the sold item using the lists from Nazm al-Zandustiti.

Core Idea
Increase in price requires the sold item to exist as a valid subject; actions that effectively destroy it invalidate the increase.

In Hanafi fiqh, increasing the price after a sale is not a new contract but an amendment to the existing one. The key condition is that the sold item must still exist in a legal sense. But what counts as 'existence'? The scholars from al-Khulasa and Nazm al-Zandustiti provide detailed lists of actions that do or do not prevent a valid increase. Understanding these distinctions is essential for proper application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that increasing the price after a sale is a valid amendment, not a new contract. The core condition is the existence of the sold item in a sense that allows a continued exchange relationship.
Contrast with increase in sold item, which is valid even after destruction.
2
Understand the condition for increase in price
The sold item must still be a valid subject for exchange (mahall li al-muqabala). Actions that destroy its legal identity (e.g., grinding wheat into flour) invalidate a later increase; actions that preserve some form or benefit (e.g., slaughtering a sheep) do not.
The condition is from the buyer's perspective: the item must remain a subject for exchange in reality (haqiqatan).
3
Study the list of 11 invalidating actions
Memorize the eleven actions from Nazm al-Zandustiti: grinding wheat, baking flour, cooking meat in certain ways, cutting meat, freeing a slave, kitaba, tadbir, making a slave-girl umm walad, spinning cotton, weaving yarn, and the death of a slave-girl.
These actions destroy the item's legal identity for price increase purposes.
4
Study the list of 12 non-invalidating actions
Memorize the twelve actions: slaughtering a sheep, carding cotton (carded or uncarded), sewing cloth into a bag without cutting, making iron into a sword, pawning or leasing a slave-girl, building or leasing a ruin, leasing land, and the scenario of second buyer meeting first seller.
These actions preserve enough of the item's form or benefit to allow a valid increase.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa is reported to allow increase after freeing a slave or similar actions, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not. The text presents both views without clear tarjih.
This ikhtilaf is recorded in al-Khulasa and the commentary.

Source Text

بخلاف الزيادة في المبيع فإنها جائزة بعد هلاكه لأنها تثبت بمقابلة الثمن وهو قائم ؛ كذا في الخلاصة . وفي الخلاصة أيضاً : وشرطها في الثمن من المشترين بقاء المبيع وكونه محلاً للمقابلة في حق المشتري حقيقة، ولو كانت جارية فأعتقها أو دبرها أو استولدها أو كاتبها أو باعها من غيره بعد القبض ثم زاد في الثمن لا يجوز، والمذكور في الكتاب قولهما وهما رويا عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجوز ولو أجرها أو رهنها أو اشترى شاة فذبحها ثم زاد في الثمن جاز بخلاف ما إذا ماتت الشاة ثم زاد في الثمن فإنه لا يجوز لأنها لم تبق محلاً للبيع بخلاف الأول حيث قام الاسم والصورة وبعض المنافع، وجملة هذا في كتاب نظم الزندوستي قال: أحد عشر شيئاً إذا فعل المشتري ثم زاد في الثمن لا يصح أولها إذا كانت حنطة فطحنها أو دقيقاً فخبزه أو لحماً فجعله قلية أو سكباجة أو جعله إرباً إرباً أو كان عبداً فأعتقه أو كاتبه أو دبره أو استولد الجارية أو قطناً فغزله أو غزلاً فنسجه الحادي عشر أو كانت جارية فماتت ولو فعل اثنتي عشر ثم زاد يجوز أولها المبيع لو كانت شاة فذبحها وإن كان قطناً محلوجاً فندفه أو غير محلوج فحلجه أو كرباساً فخاطه خريطة من غير أن يقطعه أو حديداً فجعله سيفاً أو كانت جارية فرهنها أو أجرها أو كانت خرابة فبناها أو آجرها أو آجر الأرض ثم زاد في الثمن. ومنها إذا باعها ثم إن المشتري الثاني لقي البائع الأول فزاد في الثمن جاز. ومنها المزارع إذا زاد رب الأرض السدس في نصيبه والبذر منه قبل أن يستحصده جاز وبعده لا؛ الكل في النظم اهـ. وفي تلخيص الجامع من باب ما يمنع الزيادة في الثمن : تلحق العقد مغيراً وصفه لا أصله حذار اللغو كالخيار بعد ما زاد الأصل ولداً وار (۱) وكذا قوله وتمامه فيه، ولو عبر بالعقد لأن وصف الشيء الخ. وفي الحواشي السعدية أقول: الزيادة في المكيلات والموزونات والمعدودات ليست بوصف فكيف يصح الالتحاق فيما إذا كانت مبيعة قوله : (بخلاف حط الكل) أي فلا . قال يصح . في الحواشي السعدية: يعني بطريق الالتحاق وإلا فحط الكل صحيح بطريق البرّ والصلة بالاتفاق. قوله : وترك قيداً لا بد منه الخ) قال الرملي : في حواشي المنح هكذا ذكر صاحب باللزوم بدل الصحة لكان أولى لأنها لازمة حتى لو ندم المشتري بعد ما زاد يجبر إذا امتنع كما في الخلاصة. وأطلقها فشمل ما إذا كانت من جنس الثمن أو من غيره وما إذا كانت في مجلس العقد أو بعد مدة كما في الخلاصة. وترك قيداً لا بد منه وهو قبول البائع في المجلس حتى لو زاده فلم يقبل حتى تفرقا بطلت كذا في الخلاصة وأطلق فيمن زاد فشمل المشتري ووارثه فتصح الزيادة من الورثة كما تصح من العاقدين؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وهو شامل للزيادة في المبيع أيضاً لكن يرد عليه الزيادة من الأجنبي وحاصلها كما في الخلاصة معزياً إلى الجامع الكبير : لو زاد الأجنبي فإن زاد بأمر المشتري يجب على المشتري لا على الأجنبي كالصلح، وإن زاد بغير أمره فإنه أجازه المشتري لزمته وإن لم يجز بطلت الزيادة. ولو كان حين زاد ضمن عن المشتري أو أضافها إلى مال نفسه لزمته الزيادة، ثم إن كان بأمر المشتري رجع وإلا فلا، وأما الحط فأنه جائز في جميع المواضع في موضع تجوز الزيادة وفي موضع لا تجوز اهـ . وأما الزيادة في المهر فشرطها بقاء المرأة فلو زاد فيه بعد موتها لم تصح، وأما الزيادة بعد طلاقها أو عتقها لو كانت أمة فقدمنا أحكامها في المهر ، وأما الزيادة في الأجرة بعد استيفاء بعض المعقود عليه فغير صحيحة وتجوز الزيادة في العين والمدة؛ كذا في القنية. وأما الزيادة في الرهن فسيأتي أنها صحيحه في الرهن لا في الدين. وفي الخانية من كتاب المزارعة : لو زاد أحدهما في نصيب الآخر إن كان قبل إدراك الزرع جاز مطلقاً، وإن كان بعده جاز من الذي لا بذر له لأنه حط ولا يجوز ممن البذر منه لأنه زيادة وشرطها قيام السلعة اهـ . قوله : (والزيادة في المبيع) أي وصحت ولزم البائع دفعها بشرط قبول المشتري وتلتحق أيضاً فيصير لها حصة من الثمن حتى لو هلكت الزيادة قبل القبض تسقط حصتها من الثمن بخلاف الزيادة المتولدة من المبيع حيث لا يسقط شيء بهلاكها قبل القبض، وكذا إذا زاد في الثمن عرضاً كما لو اشتراه بمائة وتقابضا ثم زاده المشتري عرضاً قيمته خمسون وهلك العرض قبل التسليم ينفسخ العقد في ثلاثة؛ كذا في القنية. وقدمنا أنه لا يشترط فيها قيام المبيع فتصح بعد هلاكه بخلاف الزيادة في الثمن وقد ذكر الزيادة في المبيع ولم يذكر الحط وذكرهما في الثمن فظاهره عدم صحة الحط من المبيع. وصرح في المحيط بأن المبيع إن كان ديناً . الحط منه، وإن كان عيناً لم يصح الحط منه لأنه إسقاط وإسقاط العين لا يصح ا هـ. قيد يصح البحر فتبعه المصنف مع ظهور الاستغناء عنه إذ الزيادة تمليك للبائع فلا تدخل في ملكه بدون قبوله بخلاف الحط فإنه إبراء وهو لا يتوقف على القبول ولو رده ارتد كما يفهم من عباراتهم في هذا المحل تأمل . قوله : (أو أبرأه عن القبض كذا في منح الغفار أيضاً قال الرملي في حاشيته عليها هكذا رأيته
Unlike increase in the sold item, it is permissible after its destruction because it is established in exchange for the price which is existing; thus in al-Khulasa. And in al-Khulasa also: Its condition in the price from the buyers is the existence of the sold item and it being a valid subject for exchange in reality regarding the buyer. If a slave-girl was set free, or made mudabbara, or made umm walad, or made a kitaba contract, or sold to another after taking possession, then increased in the price, it does not become valid. The mentioned in the book is their statement, and they narrated from Abu Hanifa that it does become valid. If he leased it, or pawned it, or bought a sheep and slaughtered it, then increased in the price, it becomes valid. Unlike if the sheep died then increased in the price, it does not become valid because it did not remain a subject for sale, unlike the first where the name, form, and some benefits remain. The summary of this is in the book Nazm al-Zandustiti: He said: Eleven things if the buyer does then increases in the price, it is not valid. First: if it was wheat and he ground it, or flour and baked it, or meat and made it into qaliya or sikhbaja, or cut it into pieces, or a slave and he set him free, or made kitaba, or made mudabbara, or a slave-girl made umm walad, or cotton and spun it, or yarn and wove it—the eleventh—or a slave-girl died. And if he does twelve things then increases, it becomes valid: first: a sheep and he slaughtered it; or if it was carded cotton and he teased it, or uncarded and he carded it, or cloth and he sewed it into a bag without cutting it, or iron and he made it into a sword, or a slave-girl and he pawned her or leased her, or a ruin and he built it, or leased it, or leased the land, then increased in the price. Among them: if he sold her, then the second buyer met the first seller and increased in the price, it becomes valid. Among them: in muzara'a, if the landowner increases the sixth in his share and the seed is from him before harvesting, it becomes valid; after, no. All in al-Nazm. End. And in Talkhis al-Jami' from the chapter of what prevents increase in price: It attaches to the contract changing its description, not its essence, to avoid futility, like an option after the thing increased has offspring etc. And similarly his statement and its completion in it, and if he expressed by the contract because the description of the thing etc. And in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diya: I say: Increase in measurable, weighable, and countable items is not a description, so how does attachment apply when they are sold? His statement: (Unlike reduction of all) meaning no. He said: valid. In al-Hawashi al-Sa'diya: Means by way of attachment, otherwise reduction of all is valid by way of righteousness and connection by agreement. His statement: And he left a necessary condition etc. Al-Ramli said in Hawashi al-Manh: Thus mentioned the author by binding instead of validity, it would be better because it is binding so that if the buyer regrets after increasing, he is compelled if he refuses, as in al-Khulasa. And he left it general, so it includes whether from the same type as the price or other, and whether in the session of contract or after a period, as in al-Khulasa. And he left a necessary condition which is acceptance of the seller in the session, so if he increased and he did not accept until they separated, it becomes void. Thus in al-Khulasa. And he left general in who increases, so it includes the buyer and his heir: increase from the heirs is valid as from the parties; thus in al-Khulasa. And it includes increase in the sold item as well, but the increase from a stranger is excluded. The summary from al-Khulasa attributed to al-Jami' al-Kabir: If a stranger increases, if he increases by order of the buyer, it is obligatory on the buyer, not on the stranger, like sulh. If he increases without his order, then if the buyer ratifies it, it becomes binding; if not, the increase is void. If at the time of increase he took responsibility for the buyer or added it to his own wealth, then the increase is binding on him. Then if it was by the buyer's order, he can recover from the buyer; otherwise no. As for reduction (hatt), it is permissible in all places where increase is permissible and where it is not. End. As for increase in dower (mahr), its condition is the existence of the woman. If he increases after her death, it is not valid. As for increase after divorce or setting free if she was a slave-girl, we have presented its rulings in the chapter of dower. As for increase in rent after some of the contracted subject matter has been used, it is not valid. And increase in the object or duration is permissible; thus in al-Qunaya. As for increase in pawn, it will come that it is valid in the pawn but not in the debt. And in al-Khaniya from the book of muzara'a: If one of them increases in the share of the other, if it is before the crop matures, it is valid absolutely; if after, it is valid from the one who has no seed because it is reduction, and not valid from the one whose seed it is because it is increase, and its condition is the existence of the commodity. End. His statement: (And increase in the sold item) i.e., it is valid, and it is binding on the seller to deliver it on condition of the buyer's acceptance, and it also attaches so it has a share of the price, so that if the increase perishes before delivery, its share of the price falls off, unlike increase generated from the sold item where nothing falls off by its destruction before delivery. Similarly, if he increased in the price by a commodity, as if he bought for a hundred and they exchanged (qabad) each other, then the buyer increased by a commodity worth fifty, and the commodity perished before delivery, the contract is dissolved in one third; thus in al-Qunaya. And we have presented that its condition is not the existence of the sold item, so it is valid after its destruction, unlike increase in the price. And he mentioned increase in the sold item and did not mention reduction, and he mentioned both in the price, so it appears that reduction from the sold item is not valid. And it is stated in al-Muhit that if the sold item is a debt, reduction from it is valid; if it is a specific 'ayn (object), reduction from it is not valid because it is an isqat (dropping) and dropping a specific 'ayn is not valid. End. A necessary condition (qayd) for validity: al-Bahr followed by the author, though it seems unnecessary because increase is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) to the seller, so it does not enter his ownership without his acceptance, unlike reduction which is ibra (release), and it does not depend on acceptance, and if he rejects it, it returns, as understood from their statements in this place. Consider. His statement: (Or he acquitted him of delivery) thus in Manh al-Ghaffar also; al-Ramli said in his hashya on it: thus I saw it.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This lengthy passage presents detailed conditions and scenarios for the validity of increase (ziyada) in the sold item and in the price, and for reduction (hatt). It begins by distinguishing increase in the sold item from increase in price: increase in the sold item is valid even after the item is destroyed because it is exchanged for the price, which still exists. The condition for increase in price is that the sold item must still exist in reality; actions that change its substance (like grinding wheat, baking flour, freeing a slave, etc.) invalidate later increase in price, while actions that preserve some form or benefit (like slaughtering a sheep, pawning, leasing) allow it. A list of eleven preventing actions and twelve allowing actions is given from Nazm al-Zandustiti. The passage also addresses increase by a stranger, increase in dower, rent, and pawn. It all clarifies that reduction (hatt) is generally permissible, but reduction from a specific 'ayn is not valid because it would be dropping ownership of a tangible thing, which is not recognized. Finally, it notes that increase requires the seller's acceptance in the session, while reduction does not, as it is a form of ibra (release). This passage is a dense compilation for scholars to memorize the rulings.

Key Terms
زيادة في الثمن (ziyada fil-thaman): Adding an extra amount to the price after the sale contract, as a voluntary amendment.
بقاء المبيع (baqa al-mabi'): Existence of the sold item in a state that makes it a valid subject for exchange.
نظم الزندوستي (Nazm al-Zandustiti): A work organizing Hanafi fiqh rules into a poetic format; the passage quotes its lists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is among the 11 actions that invalidate a later increase in price?
A) Slaughtering a sheep.
B) Leasing a slave-girl.
C) Grinding wheat.
D) Pawning a slave-girl.

Key Takeaway
A valid increase in price requires the sold item to remain as a valid subject for exchange; actions that destroy its legal identity prevent the increase, while those that preserve form or benefit do not.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
15 min
Acceptance, Stranger Increase, Reduction, and Other Contexts
Ruling on acceptance, stranger increase, reduction, and application to other contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for acceptance in increase, the rules for stranger increase, the permissibility of reduction (hatt), and the application of these rules to dower, rent, and pawn.

Core Idea
Increase requires acceptance in the session; reduction is easier as it does not require acceptance; from a specific 'ayn it is invalid.

The previous lesson focused on the condition that the sold item must exist. This lesson covers other crucial conditions: the seller's acceptance in the same session, the special case when a stranger makes an increase, and the contrasting rules for reduction (hatt). It also extends the principles to other areas of fiqh: dower (mahr), rent (ujra), pawn (rahn), and muzara'a.

Guided Path
1
Understand the acceptance condition for increase
Both parties must accept the increase in the same session; if they separate before acceptance, the increase becomes void.
This is different from reduction, which does not require acceptance.
2
Analyze increase by a stranger
If a stranger increases by order of the buyer, the obligation falls on the buyer. If without order, the buyer must ratify for it to be binding. If the stranger took responsibility or added it to his own wealth, it becomes binding on him.
The stranger cannot be forced to pay if he did not intend to be bound.
3
Study reduction (hatt) rules
Reduction is generally permissible in all cases where increase is valid or invalid, except that reduction from a specific 'ayn (tangible object) is not valid because it would be dropping ownership of a specific thing. Reduction from a debt is valid.
Reduction is considered ibra (release), which is unilateral and does not require acceptance.
4
Apply to other contexts: dower, rent, pawn
Increase in dower requires the existence of the woman; if she dies, it is invalid. Increase in rent after partial performance is invalid, but increase in the object or duration is valid. Increase in pawn is valid for the pawn itself but not for the debt.
These are extensions of the same principle.
5
Note the special case of muzara'a
In muzara'a, if one party increases the other's share, it is valid before the crop matures; after maturity, it is valid only from the one who did not provide the seed (as it is a reduction), not from the seed provider (as it is an increase requiring the crop's existence).
Shows the interaction of increase and reduction rules.

المهر ، وأما الزيادة في الأجرة بعد استيفاء بعض المعقود عليه فغير صحيحة وتجوز الزيادة في العين والمدة؛ كذا في القنية. وأما الزيادة في الرهن فسيأتي أنها صحيحه في الرهن لا في الدين. وفي الخانية من كتاب المزارعة : لو زاد أحدهما في نصيب الآخر إن كان قبل إدراك الزرع جاز مطلقاً، وإن كان بعده جاز من الذي لا بذر له لأنه حط ولا يجوز ممن البذر منه لأنه زيادة وشرطها قيام السلعة اهـ . قوله : (والزيادة في المبيع) أي وصحت ولزم البائع دفعها بشرط قبول المشتري وتلتحق أيضاً فيصير لها حصة من الثمن حتى لو هلكت الزيادة قبل القبض تسقط حصتها من الثمن بخلاف الزيادة المتولدة من المبيع حيث لا يسقط شيء بهلاكها قبل القبض، وكذا إذا زاد في الثمن عرضاً كما لو اشتراه بمائة وتقابضا ثم زاده المشتري عرضاً قيمته خمسون وهلك العرض قبل التسليم ينفسخ العقد في ثلاثة؛ كذا في القنية. وقدمنا أنه لا يشترط فيها قيام المبيع فتصح بعد هلاكه بخلاف الزيادة في الثمن وقد ذكر الزيادة في المبيع ولم يذكر الحط وذكرهما في الثمن فظاهره عدم صحة الحط من المبيع. وصرح في المحيط بأن المبيع إن كان ديناً . الحط منه، وإن كان عيناً لم يصح الحط منه لأنه إسقاط وإسقاط العين لا يصح ا هـ. قيد يصح البحر فتبعه المصنف مع ظهور الاستغناء عنه إذ الزيادة تمليك للبائع فلا تدخل في ملكه بدون قبوله بخلاف الحط فإنه إبراء وهو لا يتوقف على القبول ولو رده ارتد كما يفهم من عباراتهم في هذا المحل تأمل . قوله : (أو أبرأه عن القبض كذا في منح الغفار أيضاً قال الرملي في حاشيته عليها هكذا رأيته
Unlike increase in the sold item, it is permissible after its destruction because it is established in exchange for the price which is existing; thus in al-Khulasa. And in al-Khulasa also: Its condition in the price from the buyers is the existence of the sold item and it being a valid subject for exchange in reality regarding the buyer. If a slave-girl was set free, or made mudabbara, or made umm walad, or made a kitaba contract, or sold to another after taking possession, then increased in the price, it does not become valid. The mentioned in the book is their statement, and they narrated from Abu Hanifa that it does become valid. If he leased it, or pawned it, or bought a sheep and slaughtered it, then increased in the price, it becomes valid. Unlike if the sheep died then increased in the price, it does not become valid because it did not remain a subject for sale, unlike the first where the name, form, and some benefits remain. The summary of this is in the book Nazm al-Zandustiti: He said: Eleven things if the buyer does then increases in the price, it is not valid. First: if it was wheat and he ground it, or flour and baked it, or meat and made it into qaliya or sikhbaja, or cut it into pieces, or a slave and he set him free, or made kitaba, or made mudabbara, or a slave-girl made umm walad, or cotton and spun it, or yarn and wove it—the eleventh—or a slave-girl died. And if he does twelve things then increases, it becomes valid: first: a sheep and he slaughtered it; or if it was carded cotton and he teased it, or uncarded and he carded it, or cloth and he sewed it into a bag without cutting it, or iron and he made it into a sword, or a slave-girl and he pawned her or leased her, or a ruin and he built it, or leased it, or leased the land, then increased in the price. Among them: if he sold her, then the second buyer met the first seller and increased in the price, it becomes valid. Among them: in muzara'a, if the landowner increases the sixth in his share and the seed is from him before harvesting, it becomes valid; after, no. All in al-Nazm. End. And in Talkhis al-Jami' from the chapter of what prevents increase in price: It attaches to the contract changing its description, not its essence, to avoid futility, like an option after the thing increased has offspring etc. And similarly his statement and its completion in it, and if he expressed by the contract because the description of the thing etc. And in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diya: I say: Increase in measurable, weighable, and countable items is not a description, so how does attachment apply when they are sold? His statement: (Unlike reduction of all) meaning no. He said: valid. In al-Hawashi al-Sa'diya: Means by way of attachment, otherwise reduction of all is valid by way of righteousness and connection by agreement. His statement: And he left a necessary condition etc. Al-Ramli said in Hawashi al-Manh: Thus mentioned the author by binding instead of validity, it would be better because it is binding so that if the buyer regrets after increasing, he is compelled if he refuses, as in al-Khulasa. And he left it general, so it includes whether from the same type as the price or other, and whether in the session of contract or after a period, as in al-Khulasa. And he left a necessary condition which is acceptance of the seller in the session, so if he increased and he did not accept until they separated, it becomes void. Thus in al-Khulasa. And he left general in who increases, so it includes the buyer and his heir: increase from the heirs is valid as from the parties; thus in al-Khulasa. And it includes increase in the sold item as well, but the increase from a stranger is excluded. The summary from al-Khulasa attributed to al-Jami' al-Kabir: If a stranger increases, if he increases by order of the buyer, it is obligatory on the buyer, not on the stranger, like sulh. If he increases without his order, then if the buyer ratifies it, it becomes binding; if not, the increase is void. If at the time of increase he took responsibility for the buyer or added it to his own wealth, then the increase is binding on him. Then if it was by the buyer's order, he can recover from the buyer; otherwise no. As for reduction (hatt), it is permissible in all places where increase is permissible and where it is not. End. As for increase in dower (mahr), its condition is the existence of the woman. If he increases after her death, it is not valid. As for increase after divorce or setting free if she was a slave-girl, we have presented its rulings in the chapter of dower. As for increase in rent after some of the contracted subject matter has been used, it is not valid. And increase in the object or duration is permissible; thus in al-Qunaya. As for increase in pawn, it will come that it is valid in the pawn but not in the debt. And in al-Khaniya from the book of muzara'a: If one of them increases in the share of the other, if it is before the crop matures, it is valid absolutely; if after, it is valid from the one who has no seed because it is reduction, and not valid from the one whose seed it is because it is increase, and its condition is the existence of the commodity. End. His statement: (And increase in the sold item) i.e., it is valid, and it is binding on the seller to deliver it on condition of the buyer's acceptance, and it also attaches so it has a share of the price, so that if the increase perishes before delivery, its share of the price falls off, unlike increase generated from the sold item where nothing falls off by its destruction before delivery. Similarly, if he increased in the price by a commodity, as if he bought for a hundred and they exchanged (qabad) each other, then the buyer increased by a commodity worth fifty, and the commodity perished before delivery, the contract is dissolved in one third; thus in al-Qunaya. And we have presented that its condition is not the existence of the sold item, so it is valid after its destruction, unlike increase in the price. And he mentioned increase in the sold item and did not mention reduction, and he mentioned both in the price, so it appears that reduction from the sold item is not valid. And it is stated in al-Muhit that if the sold item is a debt, reduction from it is valid; if it is a specific 'ayn (object), reduction from it is not valid because it is an isqat (dropping) and dropping a specific 'ayn is not valid. End. A necessary condition (qayd) for validity: al-Bahr followed by the author, though it seems unnecessary because increase is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) to the seller, so it does not enter his ownership without his acceptance, unlike reduction which is ibra (release), and it does not depend on acceptance, and if he rejects it, it returns, as understood from their statements in this place. Consider. His statement: (Or he acquitted him of delivery) thus in Manh al-Ghaffar also; al-Ramli said in his hashya on it: thus I saw it.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This lengthy passage presents detailed conditions and scenarios for the validity of increase (ziyada) in the sold item and in the price, and for reduction (hatt). It begins by distinguishing increase in the sold item from increase in price: increase in the sold item is valid even after the item is destroyed because it is exchanged for the price, which still exists. The condition for increase in price is that the sold item must still exist in reality; actions that change its substance (like grinding wheat, baking flour, freeing a slave, etc.) invalidate later increase in price, while actions that preserve some form or benefit (like slaughtering a sheep, pawning, leasing) allow it. A list of eleven preventing actions and twelve allowing actions is given from Nazm al-Zandustiti. The passage also addresses increase by a stranger, increase in dower, rent, and pawn. It all clarifies that reduction (hatt) is generally permissible, but reduction from a specific 'ayn is not valid because it would be dropping ownership of a tangible thing, which is not recognized. Finally, it notes that increase requires the seller's acceptance in the session, while reduction does not, as it is a form of ibra (release). This passage is a dense compilation for scholars to memorize the rulings.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra): Acquittance; releasing someone from a liability, not requiring acceptance.
حط (hatt): Reduction in price or commodity; for price, valid; for specific 'ayn, not valid.
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; requires acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer increases the price but the seller does not accept until after they leave the meeting. What is the ruling according to the passage?
A) The increase is valid if the buyer still wants it.
B) The increase is void.
C) The increase is valid if it was in writing.
D) The increase is valid if the seller later agrees.

Key Takeaway
Increase requires acceptance in the session; reduction does not; reduction from a specific 'ayn is invalid; these rules extend to dower, rent, and pawn.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Binding Nature and Conditions of Price Increase
Explains binding nature and conditions of increasing the price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an increase in price becomes binding and identify when it becomes void.

Core Idea
A price increase binds the buyer only upon immediate acceptance by the seller in the same session.

After a sale, the buyer may voluntarily offer to pay more. Is he obliged to do so? The Hanafi school clarifies that such an increase becomes binding (lāzim) only if the seller accepts it in the same contractual session. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its indispensable conditions as recorded in al-Khulāṣa and al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that the subject is a post-contractual voluntary increase in price (ziyādah fī al-thaman). The primary ruling is that it is binding (lāzim) once conditions are met.
Binding means the buyer can be compelled to pay the extra amount.
2
Determine the condition of acceptance
The seller must accept the increase in the same session. Without that, the increase is void.
Acceptance after separation invalidates the increase.
3
Consider who can validly increase
The increase is valid from the buyer, his heir, or any third party (subject to rules).
This lesson focuses on the buyer/heir; third-party rules are covered separately.
4
Note the effect of separation before acceptance
If the buyer offers an increase and the seller does not accept until they separate, the increase becomes bāṭil (void).
Separation ends the offer window.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باللزوم بدل الصحة لكان أولى لأنها لازمة حتى لو ندم المشتري بعد ما زاد يجبر إذا امتنع كما في الخلاصة. وأطلقها فشمل ما إذا كانت من جنس الثمن أو من غيره وما إذا كانت في مجلس العقد أو بعد مدة كما في الخلاصة. وترك قيداً لا بد منه وهو قبول البائع في المجلس حتى لو زاده فلم يقبل حتى تفرقا بطلت كذا في الخلاصة وأطلق فيمن زاد فشمل المشتري ووارثه فتصح الزيادة من الورثة كما تصح من العاقدين؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وهو شامل للزيادة في المبيع أيضاً لكن يرد عليه الزيادة من الأجنبي وحاصلها كما في الخلاصة معزياً إلى الجامع الكبير : لو زاد الأجنبي فإن زاد بأمر المشتري يجب على المشتري لا على الأجنبي كالصلح، وإن زاد بغير أمره فإنه أجازه المشتري لزمته وإن لم يجز بطلت الزيادة. ولو كان حين زاد ضمن عن المشتري أو أضافها إلى مال نفسه لزمته الزيادة، ثم إن كان بأمر المشتري رجع وإلا فلا، وأما الحط فأنه جائز في جميع المواضع في موضع تجوز الزيادة وفي موضع لا تجوز اهـ . وأما الزيادة في المهر فشرطها بقاء المرأة فلو زاد فيه بعد موتها لم تصح، وأما الزيادة بعد طلاقها أو عتقها لو كانت أمة فقدمنا أحكامها في المهر ، وأما الزيادة في الأجرة بعد استيفاء بعض المعقود عليه فغير صحيحة وتجوز الزيادة في العين والمدة؛ كذا في القنية. وأما الزيادة في الرهن فسيأتي أنها صحيحه في الرهن لا في الدين. وفي الخانية من كتاب المزارعة : لو زاد أحدهما في نصيب الآخر إن كان قبل إدراك الزرع جاز مطلقاً، وإن كان بعده جاز من الذي لا بذر له لأنه حط ولا يجوز ممن البذر منه لأنه زيادة وشرطها قيام السلعة اهـ .
With binding rather than validity, it would be more appropriate because it is binding, so that if the buyer regrets after increasing, he is forced if he refuses, as in al-Khulasa. And it was general, so it includes whether the increase is of the same type as the price or otherwise, and whether it is in the session or after a period, as in al-Khulasa. And it omitted an indispensable condition: the acceptance of the seller in the session, so that if he increases and the seller does not accept until they separate, it becomes void, as stated in al-Khulasa. And it was general concerning who increases, so it includes the buyer and his heir; the increase from heirs is valid just as from the contracting parties, as in al-Khulasa. And it includes increase in the sold object as well, but it is countered by increase from a third party. Its summary as in al-Khulasa, citing al-Jami' al-Kabir: If a third party increases, if he increases by the order of the buyer, it is binding on the buyer, not on the third party, like conciliation (sulh). If he increases without his order, if the buyer ratifies it, it becomes binding on him; if not, the increase becomes void. If when he increased he guaranteed on behalf of the buyer or attributed it to his own wealth, the increase is binding on him. Then if it was by the buyer's order, he has recourse, otherwise not. As for reduction (hatt), it is permissible in all cases, in a place where increase is permissible and where it is not. End. As for increase in the dower, its condition is the survival of the woman; if he increases after her death, it is invalid. As for increase after her divorce or her emancipation if she was a slave, we have presented its rulings in the chapter on dower. As for increase in the hire (ujrah) after partial performance of the contract, it is invalid, but increase in the object or the duration is permissible, as stated in al-Qunyah. As for increase in the pawn (rahn), it will come that it is valid regarding the pawn, not the debt. And in al-Khaniyyah from the book of sharecropping: If one of them increases in the share of the other, if it is before the harvest, it is valid absolutely; if after, it is valid from the one who has no seed because it is reduction, and invalid from the one who has the seed because it is increase, and its condition is the existence of the commodity. End.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings on increase (ziyadah) in the price (thaman) from various sources, particularly al-Khulasa and al-Jami' al-Kabir. The author clarifies that the increase in price is binding (lazim) once accepted by the seller in the same session; if the seller does not accept until they separate, the increase becomes void. The increase can come from the buyer, his heir, or even a third party. If a third party increases with the buyer's authorization, it binds the buyer; without authorization, it becomes binding only if the buyer later ratifies it. However, if the third party explicitly guarantees or attributes the increase to his own wealth, it binds him personally. The passage then briefly discusses increase in other contexts: dower (mahr) requires the woman's survival; hire (ujrah) cannot be increased after partial performance, but the object or duration may be increased; pawn (rahn) increase is valid only in the pawn itself, not the debt; and in sharecropping (muzara'ah), increase before harvest is valid, but after harvest it is treated as reduction (hatt) from those without seed. The overall principle is that increase in price is a transfer of ownership to the seller, requiring his acceptance, whereas reduction (hatt) is a form of remission (isqat) that does not require acceptance.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyādah): An addition to the price or sold object after the contract, treated as a new offer.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid for the sold object.
لزوم (luzūm): Binding nature; after acceptance the increase is compulsory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the crucial condition for a price increase to be binding?
A) The increase must be in writing.
B) The seller must accept in the same session.
C) The buyer must pay immediately.
D) The increase must be at least 10%.

Key Takeaway
A buyer's voluntary price increase binds him only if the seller accepts it in the same contractual session.
