10 min
Third Party Increase in Price
Explains rulings for third party increase in price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine who bears the obligation when a third party increases the price, based on authorization, ratification, and express guarantee.

Core Idea
A third party's price increase binds the buyer only if authorized; otherwise it requires ratification, but can bind the third party personally if guaranteed.

What happens when a stranger, not the buyer, offers to pay more? The Hanafi school provides detailed rules: the increase may bind the buyer, the third party, or become void depending on authorization, ratification, and guarantee. This lesson, based on al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr via al-Khulāṣa, clarifies the distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third party's action
Recognise that a third party (ajnabī) increases the price on a sold item.
Third party means someone other than buyer and seller.
2
Check if the third party acted with buyer's order
If the third party increases by the buyer's instruction (amr), the increase binds the buyer, not the third party.
The third party is like an agent; the buyer must pay.
3
If without order, check buyer's ratification
If the third party acts without the buyer's order, the buyer can later accept (ratify) the increase. If ratified, it binds the buyer; if not, the increase is void.
Ratification is retrospective acceptance.
4
Consider if the third party guaranteed or attributed to self
If the third party explicitly guarantees payment (ḍamān) or attributes the increase to his own wealth (ḍamma ilā mālihī), the increase binds the third party personally.
In that case, the third party is directly liable.
5
Note the rule for reduction (ḥaṭṭ)?
Reduction (lowering the price) is always permissible unlike increase, which requires conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
أجنبي (ajnabī): A third party not involved in the original contract.
ضمان (ḍamān): Guarantee; express assumption of liability.
حط (ḥaṭṭ): Reduction or abatement of the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a third party increases the price without buyer's order and the buyer does not ratify, the increase is:
A) Binding on the third party.
B) Binding on the buyer.
C) Void.
D) Converted into a gift.

Key Takeaway
A third party's price increase is void unless authorized by the buyer, ratified by the buyer, or guaranteed by the third party.

Increase in Dower, Hire, Pawn, and Sharecropping
Summarizes conditional rulings for increase in various contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific conditions for a valid increase in four different contracts: marriage (mahr), hire (ujrah), pawn (rahn), and sharecropping (muzara'ah).

Core Idea
Increase in a contract's subject matter is valid only if the subject of the contract still exists and the contract is still open.

The ruling on increase is not limited to sales. The Hanafi school extends the principle to other contracts with specific conditions. This lesson synthesizes rulings from al-Qunyah, al-Khāniyyah, and earlier sections, explaining when an increase in dower, hire, pawn, or sharecropping is valid or invalid.

Guided Path
1
Examine increase in dower (mahr)
The husband may increase the dower after marriage, but the wife must be alive. If she dies, the increase is invalid.
Also valid after divorce or emancipation? Referenced to earlier chapter.
2
Examine increase in hire (ujrah)
After partial performance of the hiring contract, an increase in the hire fee is invalid. However, increasing the hired object or duration is valid.
Increase in fee is like a new contract requiring fresh consent.
3
Examine increase in pawn (rahn)
Increasing the pawn itself (the collateral) is valid; increasing the debt is not.
Details promised in later section on rahn.
4
Examine increase in sharecropping (muzara'ah)
If one party increases the other's share before harvest, it is valid absolutely. After harvest, it is valid only from the party without seed (as it is a reduction), but invalid from the party with seed (as it is an increase without the commodity existing).
Condition for increase: the commodity (crop) must still exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

With binding rather than validity, it would be more appropriate because it is binding, so that if the buyer regrets after increasing, he is forced if he refuses, as in al-Khulasa. And it was general, so it includes whether the increase is of the same type as the price or otherwise, and whether it is in the session or after a period, as in al-Khulasa. And it omitted an indispensable condition: the acceptance of the seller in the session, so that if he increases and the seller does not accept until they separate, it becomes void, as stated in al-Khulasa. And it was general concerning who increases, so it includes the buyer and his heir; the increase from heirs is valid just as from the contracting parties, as in al-Khulasa. And it includes increase in the sold object as well, but it is countered by increase from a third party. Its summary as in al-Khulasa, citing al-Jami' al-Kabir: If a third party increases, if he increases by the order of the buyer, it is binding on the buyer, not on the third party, like conciliation (sulh). If he increases without his order, if the buyer ratifies it, it becomes binding on him; if not, the increase becomes void. If when he increased he guaranteed on behalf of the buyer or attributed it to his own wealth, the increase is binding on him. Then if it was by the buyer's order, he has recourse, otherwise not. As for reduction (hatt), it is permissible in all cases, in a place where increase is permissible and where it is not. End. As for increase in the dower, its condition is the survival of the woman; if he increases after her death, it is invalid. As for increase after her divorce or her emancipation if she was a slave, we have presented its rulings in the chapter on dower. As for increase in the hire (ujrah) after partial performance of the contract, it is invalid, but increase in the object or the duration is permissible, as stated in al-Qunyah. As for increase in the pawn (rahn), it will come that it is valid regarding the pawn, not the debt. And in al-Khaniyyah from the book of sharecropping: If one of them increases in the share of the other, if it is before the harvest, it is valid absolutely; if after, it is valid from the one who has no seed because it is reduction, and invalid from the one who has the seed because it is increase, and its condition is the existence of the commodity. End.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings on increase (ziyadah) in the price (thaman) from various sources, particularly al-Khulasa and al-Jami' al-Kabir. The author clarifies that the increase in price is binding (lazim) once accepted by the seller in the same session; if the seller does not accept until they separate, the increase becomes void. The increase can come from the buyer, his heir, or even a third party. If a third party increases with the buyer's authorization, it binds the buyer; without authorization, it becomes binding only if the buyer later ratifies it. However, if the third party explicitly guarantees or attributes the increase to his own wealth, it binds him personally. The passage then briefly discusses increase in other contexts: dower (mahr) requires the woman's survival; hire (ujrah) cannot be increased after partial performance, but the object or duration may be increased; pawn (rahn) increase is valid only in the pawn itself, not the debt; and in sharecropping (muzara'ah), increase before harvest is valid, but after harvest it is treated as reduction (hatt) from those without seed. The overall principle is that increase in price is a transfer of ownership to the seller, requiring his acceptance, whereas reduction (hatt) is a form of remission (isqat) that does not require acceptance.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): Dower or bridal gift in marriage.
أجرة (ujrah): Hire fee or rent.
رهن (rahn): Pawn or collateral.
مزارعة (muzāraʿah): Sharecropping contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sharecropping contract, an increase in one party's share after harvest is valid if it comes from which party?
A) The party who provided seed.
B) The party who did not provide seed.
C) Either party.
D) Neither party.

Key Takeaway
Increase in a contract is valid only when the contract's subject exists and, for fee contracts, before performance; otherwise it is invalid or treated as reduction.

Increase in the Sold Object and Reduction of Price
Commentary on increase and reduction in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increase in the sold object and distinguish between valid and invalid reductions.

Core Idea
Increase in the sold object requires buyer acceptance; reduction of a specific object is invalid as it is a remission of a tangible thing.

In sale contracts, parties may later agree to add items to the sold object or reduce the price. The Hanafi school establishes distinct rules for these modifications. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies when an increase becomes binding and why reduction of a specific object, unlike reduction of a debt, is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modifications
The passage discusses two scenarios: increase in the sold object (ziyadah fi al-mabi') and reduction (hatt) of the sold object. Note that reduction is only addressed after noting that it was not mentioned in the base text.
Reduction of price is valid by default; the focus is on reduction of the sold object.
2
Condition for increase
For an increase in the sold object to be valid, the buyer must accept it. If accepted, the seller is obliged to deliver the increase, and it acquires a share of the price. If the increase perishes before delivery, its share of the price abates.
This differs from natural increase (e.g., fruit) where no abatement occurs.
3
Distinguish reduction of specific object vs. debt
Reduction (hatt) of the sold object is invalid if the object is a specific tangible item ('ayn), because it is a remission (isqat) of a tangible thing, which is not allowed. However, if the sold object is a debt (dayn), reduction is valid.
The underlying principle: reduction of a specific object is like giving away ownership without consideration, which is not permissible in sale.
4
Understand the legal nature
Increase is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) to the seller, so it requires the seller's acceptance. Reduction is a discharge (ibra') and does not require acceptance, but it is restricted to debts because tangible items cannot be remitted.
The commentator notes this subtlety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والزيادة في المبيع) أي وصحت ولزم البائع دفعها بشرط قبول المشتري وتلتحق أيضاً فيصير لها حصة من الثمن حتى لو هلكت الزيادة قبل القبض تسقط حصتها من الثمن بخلاف الزيادة المتولدة من المبيع حيث لا يسقط شيء بهلاكها قبل القبض، وكذا إذا زاد في الثمن عرضاً كما لو اشتراه بمائة وتقابضا ثم زاده المشتري عرضاً قيمته خمسون وهلك العرض قبل التسليم ينفسخ العقد في ثلاثة؛ كذا في القنية. وقدمنا أنه لا يشترط فيها قيام المبيع فتصح بعد هلاكه بخلاف الزيادة في الثمن وقد ذكر الزيادة في المبيع ولم يذكر الحط وذكرهما في الثمن فظاهره عدم صحة الحط من المبيع. وصرح في المحيط بأن المبيع إن كان ديناً . الحط منه، وإن كان عيناً لم يصح الحط منه لأنه إسقاط وإسقاط العين لا يصح ا هـ. قيد يصح البحر فتبعه المصنف مع ظهور الاستغناء عنه إذ الزيادة تمليك للبائع فلا تدخل في ملكه بدون قبوله بخلاف الحط فإنه إبراء وهو لا يتوقف على القبول ولو رده ارتد كما يفهم من عباراتهم في هذا المحل تأمل .
His statement: (And increase in the sold object) i.e., it is valid and the seller is obliged to deliver it on condition of the buyer's acceptance, and it becomes attached, so it acquires a share of the price such that if the increase perishes before delivery, its share of the price abates, unlike an increase generated from the sold object where nothing abates with its destruction before delivery. Similarly, if he increase in the price with a commodity, such as if he bought it for one hundred and they exchanged receipts, then the buyer increased with a commodity worth fifty, and the commodity perished before delivery, the contract is rescinded in three [cases?]; as in al-Qunyah. And we have stated that the existence of the sold object is not required for the increase, so it is valid after its destruction, unlike increase in the price. And he mentioned increase in the sold object but did not mention reduction (hatt), while he mentioned both regarding the price, so its apparent meaning is that reduction from the sold object is not valid. And al-Muhit states: if the sold object is a debt, reduction from it is valid; if it is a specific object, reduction is not valid because it is a remission (isqat), and remission of a specific object is not valid. End. Al-Bahr restricts [something], and the author followed him despite apparent self-sufficiency because increase is a transfer of ownership to the seller, so it does not enter his ownership without his acceptance, unlike reduction which is a discharge (ibra') and does not depend on acceptance; even if he rejects it, it is rejected, as understood from their expressions in this place. Consider.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'And increase in the sold object'. The commentator explains that when a buyer increases the sold object (e.g., adds an extra item to the sale), the increase becomes part of the sale and the seller must deliver it, provided the buyer accepts. The increase has a proportional share of the price, so if it perishes before delivery, the buyer is entitled to a reduction in the price corresponding to that share. This is distinguished from a natural increase (like fruit growing on the sold tree) where no price reduction occurs if it perishes before delivery. The passage also discusses the case where the buyer increases the price with a commodity (instead of cash) and that commodity perishes before delivery: the contract is rescinded in three cases (details in the source text). A key point is that increase in the sold object does not require the object's existence at the time of increase; it can be done after the object perishes. This differs from increase in the price, which does require the price to be existing. The text then addresses reduction (hatt) of the sold object: it is invalid because a specific object cannot be remitted (isqat). However, if the sold object is a debt (dayn), reduction is valid because a debt can be remitted. The commentator adds a nuance: increase requires the seller's acceptance because it is a transfer of ownership, while reduction is a discharge (ibra') and does not require acceptance.

Key Terms
زيادة في المبيع (ziyādah fī al-mabīʿ): An addition to the sold object after the contract, which becomes part of the sale and requires the buyer's acceptance.
حط (ḥaṭṭ): Reduction or remission of part of the price or the sold object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer adds a new item to the sold object (increase in mabi'), what condition is required for the increase to be valid?
A) The seller's acceptance in the same session.
B) The buyer's acceptance.
C) The original sold object must still exist.
D) The increase must be of the same type as the price.

Key Takeaway
Increase in the sold object is valid with the buyer's acceptance; reduction of a specific object is invalid, but reduction of a debt is valid.

Types of Ibra' After Payment: The Remaining Debt in Hanafi Law
Clarifies types of discharge after payment and the effect on debt and mortgage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between barā'at qabd (discharge by receipt) and barā'at isqāṭ (discharge by remission) and state the legal consequences of each after payment.

Core Idea
Discharge after payment is valid because the debt remains in the buyer's liability; its type determines whether the seller must return the price.

This is a close examination of a nuanced ruling in sales: what happens when the seller waives the price after the buyer has already paid? The text from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq, drawing on al-Dhakhira and other authorities, explains that the debt persists in abstract form, so a post-payment waiver is possible. However, the type of discharge matters—whether it is by receipt (istifa') or by remission (isqat)—and the default interpretation is a key point of dispute within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Note that the seller is discharging the buyer from the price after the buyer has already paid. This is a post-payment waiver.
The passage distinguishes this from pre-payment waiver (hatt).
2
Distinguish the two types of ibra'
Ibra' is of two types: barā'at qabd (discharge by receipt/taking) and barā'at isqāṭ (discharge by remission). The former confirms payment; the latter remits the debt.
Hiba (gift) and hatt (reduction) are only isqat, not divided into two types.
3
Apply the default rule for unspecified ibra'
If the seller says 'I have discharged you' without qualification, it is interpreted as the first type (istifa'), which does not require the seller to return the price.
This is because the lesser form (istifa') is presumed, as per the text.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Shaykh al-Islam (al-Sarakhsi?) differed on whether ibra' after payment is always equivalent to isqat, obliging return. The text advises caution (tatammul) when giving fatwa.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view distinguishing types, but the ikhtilaf is recognized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ووجب على البائع مثل ذلك للمشتري، ولو أبرأه عن البعض بعد القبض لا يصح وكان يجب أن لا تصح والحط بعد القبض أيضاً كالإبراء لأن المشتري قد برئ من الثمن بالإيفاء والهبة والحط لم يصادف ديناً قائماً في ذمة القضاء. وإنما لم يصح الإبراء لأن الإبراء على نوعين براءة قبض واستيفاء وبراءة إسقاط . فإذا أطلق حمل على الأوّل لأنه أقل كأنه نص عليه وقال أبرأتك براءة قبض واستيفاء وفيه لا يرجع. ولو قال أبرأتك براءة إسقاط صح ووجب على البائع رد ما قبض من المشتري بخلاف الهبة والحط لا يتنوّع إلى نوعين وإنما هي اسقاط ، وإذا وهب كل الدين أو حط أو أبرأه منه فهو على ما ذكرنا هذا جملة ما أورده شيخ الإسلام في شرح كتاب الشفعة وفي شرح كتاب الرهن. وذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي في الباب الثاني في شرح كتاب الرهن أن الإبراء راء المضاف إلى الثمن بعد الاستيفاء صحيح حتى يجب على البائع رد ما قبض من المشتري وسوى بين الإبراء والهبة والحط فيتأمل عند الفتوى واختلفوا فيما إذا أبرأه ولم يعين أنها إسقاط أو استيفاء. فإن قلت : هل لبقاء الدين بعد ايفائه فائدة أخرى؟ قلت: نعم لو كان بالدين رهن ثم قضاه الدين ثم هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن هلك His statement: (Or he discharged him from the receipt) as in Manh al-Ghaffar also. Al-Ramli said in his gloss on it: 'This is how I saw it with the sold object, the gift, because the increase in the wife...' [?] As for the increase in the wife, like if he married him a slave-woman and then increased him another, it is invalid, unlike increase in the dower. And he was general in reduction (hatt) of the price, so it includes whether it is before or after its receipt. If he reduces after he has paid the price or discharged him, al-Dhakhira says: If some of the price goes from the buyer before receipt or he discharges him from receipt, it is reduction. And if after receipt he then reduces the sale or gifts it, it is valid and the seller must give the like to the buyer. If he discharges him from some of it after receipt, it is invalid, and it would be necessary that it be invalid. Reduction after receipt is also like discharge because the buyer has been cleared of the price by payment, and the gift and reduction do not encounter a standing debt in the buyer's liability. The answer is that the debt remains in the buyer's liability after payment because he did not pay the specific obligatory thing so that it would not remain in the liability; he paid its like, so what was in his liability remains as it was, except that the buyer is not demanded because he has the like against the seller by payment. If the seller demands the buyer for the price, the buyer can also demand the seller, so the demand of each does not benefit. Thus it is known that the price remains in the buyer's liability after payment, and the gift and reduction encounter a standing debt in the buyer's liability after payment. The discharge is not valid because discharge is of two types: discharge of receipt and taking (barā'at qabd wa istīfā') and discharge of remission (barā'at isqāṭ). If it is general, it is taken as the first because it is lesser, as if he specified and said 'I have discharged you with a discharge of receipt and taking', and in that there is no recourse. If he says 'I have discharged you with a discharge of remission', it is valid and the seller must return what he took from the buyer, unlike gift and reduction. Gift and reduction are not divided into two types; they are only remission. If he gives the entire debt as a gift or reduces it or discharges him from it, it is as we mentioned. This is the summary of what Shaykh al-Islam presented in the commentary on the chapter of preemption and in the commentary on the chapter of pledge. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in the second chapter of the commentary on the book of pledge that the discharge added to the price after payment is valid, so the seller must return what he took from the buyer, and he equated discharge, gift, and reduction. So one must reflect at the time of fatwa. And they differed concerning when he discharges him without specifying whether it is isqat or istifa'. If you say: Is there any other benefit to the debt remaining after payment? I say: Yes, if there is a mortgage on the debt and then he pays off the debt, and then the mortgage perishes in the hands of the mortgagee, it perishes as a debt, and he must return what was taken, unlike if he discharged him and then it perished. Al-Zayla'i said in his chapter: The difference is that discharge (ibra') extinguishes the debt entirely, while by payment it does not extinguish because the cause of the debt remains. And we have written in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya from the book, in his handwriting and the handwriting of the author of al-Bahr, and it is a slip of the pen of the author of al-Bahr, so the author followed him in it; the correct is 'or he discharged him from some part'. End. I say: Such is the expression of al-Dhakhira, its text: 'or he discharged him from some of the price before receipt'. His statement: 'So one must reflect at the time of fatwa' – this is from the expression of al-Dhakhira. And his statement: 'and they differed, etc.' – he should have mentioned it with fa' to be an explanation of the summary he presented: that the difference is in the case of non-specification. Al-Nahr said: And from this it is known that there is no disagreement regarding the return of the driver [of payment] of what he paid if he discharged him with a discharge of remission, and regarding the non-return if he discharged him with a discharge of receipt, and that the general [case]... And upon this is derived: if he suspended her divorce on her discharging him from the dower, and then he paid her, it does not invalidate the difference, and it is...
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the validity of ibra' (discharge) from the price after the buyer has paid it. The text begins by noting a phrase from the matn: 'or he discharged him from the receipt', and then comments on it. The core issue is whether the seller can validly waive the remaining price after payment has been made. The initial view from al-Dhakhira is that reduction (hatt) or gift of the price after payment is valid because the debt remains in the buyer's liability even after payment. This is because when a person pays a debt, he pays a substitute (mithl) of what was owed, not the exact same coins (unless specified). So the debt in the abstract remains in the buyer's liability, but he cannot be sued for it because he has a reciprocal claim against the seller (the seller owes him the price once paid). This mutual offset means each cannot effectively demand from the other. Thus, when the seller reduces or gives a gift of the price after payment, it is valid because it encounters a standing debt. However, ibra' (discharge) has two types: (1) barā'at qabd wa istīfā' (discharge by receipt and taking) – which is the confirmation that the debt has been paid and the seller has received it; this does not entail return of the price. (2) barā'at isqāṭ (discharge by remission) – which is a waiver of the debt, requiring the seller to return what he took. If the seller says 'I have discharged you' without specifying, it is understood as type (1) by default. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi authorities: Shaykh al-Islam and al-Sarakhsi differed on whether ibra' after payment is valid at all; al-Sarakhsi considered it valid and obliged the seller to return the price, equating ibra' with hiba and hatt. The text recommends caution (tatammul) when giving fatwa. A practical application: if a debt is secured by a mortgage (rahn), and the debtor pays off the debt, then the mortgage perishes in the hands of the mortgagee, the mortgagee is liable for the value of the mortgage because the debt is considered extinguished by payment? Actually the passage contrasts: if the debtor pays off the debt and then the mortgage perishes, the mortgagee must return the mortgage value; but if the debtor is discharged by ibra' and then the mortgage perishes, the mortgagee does not need to return because the debt is extinguished from the start. The passage ends with a discussion about ambiguity in specifying the type of ibra' and the effect on a divorce conditional on ibra'.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibrāʾ): Discharge from a debt; of two types: barā'at qabd (discharge by receipt) and barā'at isqāṭ (discharge by remission).
إسقاط (isqāṭ): Remission of a debt, which extinguishes it completely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the seller tells the buyer after payment 'I have discharged you from the price' without specifying, what is the default interpretation?
A) It is a discharge by remission (isqat), requiring the seller to return the price.
B) It is a discharge by receipt (istifa'), and the buyer has no recourse.
C) It is invalid because the debt has been paid.
D) It is a gift, and the buyer must return the gift.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between discharge by receipt and discharge by remission determines whether the seller must return the price after post-payment ibra'.

The Validity of Discount and Release After Payment in Hanafi Fiqh
Explains ruling of discount and release after payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on discount (hatt) and release (ibra') after payment and distinguish between valid and invalid forms of release.

Core Idea
Discount after payment is valid; release is invalid unless specified as discharge.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a common transaction issue: after a buyer pays in full, can the seller discount or release part of the price? The Hanafi school distinguishes between discount/gift and release, with a crucial nuance about the type of release. We'll unpack the reasoning and the practical fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
Determine whether the discount or release occurs before or after receipt of payment. The ruling depends on this timing.
The passage focuses on after payment (ba‘da al-qabd).
2
State the ruling for discount and gift
If after payment the seller discounts or gifts part of the price, it is valid and the seller must return the equivalent amount to the buyer.
This is based on reasoning that the debt remains in the buyer's liability.
3
State the ruling for release (ibra')
If the seller releases the buyer from part of the price after payment without specifying the type, it is invalid. Only if the seller explicitly says 'barā'at isqāt' (release of discharge) does it become valid and obligate return.
The default interpretation of absolute release is 'barā'at qabd wa istifā'' (acknowledgment of receipt).
4
Understand the reasoning (ta'līl)
After payment, the debt remains because the buyer paid the equivalent, not the exact same coins. Thus discount and gift encounter an existing debt. Release, however, is ambiguous: the default meaning is acknowledgment, which has no effect after actual payment.
This reasoning explains why discount/gift are valid but absolute release is not.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imām al-Sarakhsī equated release with gift and discount, making all valid after payment. However, the later scholars (muftā bihī) maintain the distinction, requiring specification for release.
The muftā bihī is the latter view, as stated in al-Dhakhira and al-Bahr.

Source Text

والحط لا يتنوّع إلى نوعين وإنما هي اسقاط ، وإذا وهب كل الدين أو حط أو أبرأه منه فهو على ما ذكرنا هذا جملة ما أورده شيخ الإسلام في شرح كتاب الشفعة وفي شرح كتاب الرهن. وذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي في الباب الثاني في شرح كتاب الرهن أن الإبراء راء المضاف إلى الثمن بعد الاستيفاء صحيح حتى يجب على البائع رد ما قبض من المشتري وسوى بين الإبراء والهبة والحط فيتأمل عند الفتوى واختلفوا فيما إذا أبرأه ولم يعين أنها إسقاط أو استيفاء. فإن قلت : هل لبقاء الدين بعد ايفائه فائدة أخرى؟ قلت: نعم لو كان بالدين رهن ثم قضاه الدين ثم هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن هلك بالدين ووجب عليه رد المقبوض بخلاف ما لو أبرأه ثم هلك قال الزيلعي في بابه والفرق أن الإبراء يسقط به الدين أصلاً وبالاستيفاء لا يسقط لقيام الموجب للدين وقد كتبنا في الفوائد الفقهية من كتاب في خطه وخط صاحب البحر وهو سبق قلم من صاحب البحر فتبعه المؤلف فيه، والصواب أو أبرأه عن البعض اهـ . قلت : وهكذا عبارة الذخيرة ونصها أو أبرأه عن بعض الثمن قبل القبض . قوله : (فيتأمل عند الفتوى هذا من عبارة الذخيرة وقوله واختلفوا الخ الأولى ذكره بالفاء ليكون بياناً ما لو علق طلاقها بإبرائها عن المهر ثم دفعه لها لا يبطل الخلاف
Book of Sales, Chapter of Murabaha and Tawliyah. With the sold item, gift, because the increase in the spouse is like when he married a slave girl and then added another, it is not valid, unlike the increase in the dowry. And he [the author] made absolute in the discount from the price, so it includes whether it is before or after receipt. So if he discounts after he paid the price or released him, he said in al-Dhakhira: If some of the price from the buyer disappeared before receipt or he released him from receipt, it is a discount. And if after receipt he then discounts the sale or gives a gift, it is valid and the seller is obliged to give similar to the buyer. And if he released him from part after receipt, it is not valid. And it would have to be invalid, and the discount after receipt is also like release because the buyer has become free from the price by payment, and gift and discount did not encounter an existing debt in the buyer's liability. The answer is that the debt remains in the buyer's liability after payment because he did not pay the exact obligation so that it would not remain in the liability; rather he paid its equivalent, so what is in his liability remains as it was, except that the buyer is not demanded because he has a similar claim against the seller by payment. So if the seller demands the buyer for the price, the buyer can also demand the seller, so the demand of each one is futile. Thus it is known that the price remains in the buyer's liability after payment, and gift and discount encountered an existing debt in the buyer's liability after payment. However, the release is not valid because release is of two types: release of receipt and collection, and release of discharge. If it is absolute, it is interpreted as the first because it is less, as if he explicitly said: I release you with a release of receipt and collection, in which case he does not reclaim. And if he said: I release you with a release of discharge, it is valid and the seller must return what he received from the buyer, unlike gift and discount which are not divided into two types but are only discharge. And if he gifted the entire debt or discounted it or released him from it, it is as we mentioned. This is the summary of what Shaykh al-Islam presented in his commentary on the Chapter of Shuf'a and in his commentary on the Chapter of Rahn. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in the second chapter of his commentary on the Chapter of Rahn that the release attached to the price after receipt is valid so that the seller must return what he received from the buyer, and he equated release, gift, and discount, so it is to be pondered upon at the time of issuing fatwa. And they differed concerning the case where he released him without specifying whether it is discharge or collection. So if you ask: Is there any other benefit to the debt remaining after payment? I say: Yes, if there was a pledge for the debt and then he paid the debt and then the pledge perished in the hand of the pledgee, it perishes for the debt and he must return the sum received, unlike if he released him and then it perished. Al-Zayla'i said in his chapter: The difference is that release extinguishes the debt fundamentally, while by collection it is not extinguished because the cause of the debt remains. And we have written in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya from the book: In his handwriting and the handwriting of the author of al-Bahr, which is a slip of the pen from the author of al-Bahr, and the author followed him in it; the correct is 'or he released him from part of it.' I say: Thus is the expression of al-Dhakhira: 'or he released him from part of the price before receipt.' His saying: (So it is to be pondered at the time of fatwa) this is from the expression of al-Dhakhira, and his saying 'and they differed etc.' The first should be mentioned with fa' to be an explanation of what was presented, that the difference is in the case of non-specification. Al-Nahr said: It is understood from this that there is no disagreement regarding the return of the payer of what he paid if he released him with a release of discharge, and regarding no return if he released him with a release of collection, and that the absolute [is interpreted as collection]. And on this branches the case where he conditioned her divorce on her releasing him from the dowry and then he paid it to her, the divorce does not become invalid.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the effect of discount (حط) and release (إبراء) from the price in a sale after payment. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the positions from al-Dhakhira and other works. He begins by noting that the ruling on discount applies whether it is before or after receipt of payment. If the buyer pays the full price and then the seller discounts part of it, this is valid and the seller must return the discounted amount to the buyer. Similarly, if the seller gives a gift of part of the price, it is valid. However, if the seller releases the buyer from part of the price after payment, this release is not valid unless it is explicitly specified as a release of discharge (براءة إسقاط). The reasoning is that after payment, the debt remains in the buyer's liability because he paid the equivalent, not the exact same coins. But the buyer cannot be compelled to pay again because he has a claim against the seller. The release is not valid because the default interpretation of release is release of receipt and collection (براءة قبض واستيفاء), which would mean the seller admits he received payment, but that does not require return of money. Only a release of discharge extinguishes the debt and obligates the seller to return the payment. The passage ends with a note from al-Nahr that there is agreement on the ruling when the type is specified, and the disagreement is only when it is absolute. A practical application is given: if a husband conditions his wife's divorce on her releasing him from the dower, and then he pays her, the divorce does not become invalid (i.e., the release is effective as discharge).

Key Terms
حط (hatt): Discount or reduction from the price.
إبراء (ibra'): Release from a debt; has two types: release of receipt/collection and release of discharge.
براءة قبض واستيفاء (bara'at qabd wa istifa'): Release meaning the creditor acknowledges receipt of payment; does not obligate return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a seller releasing the buyer from part of the price after the buyer has paid in full?
A) The release is valid and the seller must return the amount.
B) The release is invalid unless the seller specifies 'release of discharge'.
C) The release is valid and the seller does not need to return anything.
D) The release is invalid because the debt is extinguished.

Key Takeaway
Discount and gift after payment are valid and obligate the seller to refund; release is only valid if explicitly designated as discharge.

Ruling on Increase in the Sold Item
Explains ruling on increase in sold item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on increase in the sold item and identify its effect on the buyer's right to possession and the seller's right to detain.

Core Idea
Increase in the sold item attaches to the contract — the buyer cannot take possession without paying for it.

This lesson examines the principle that an increase in the sold item (زيادة في المبيع) made after the contract becomes part of the sale. The buyer must pay the additional amount, and the seller may detain the item until payment. This ruling also affects claims by third parties and returns due to defects or options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? The seller adds an increase to the sold item after the contract. The ruling: the increase is part of the contract and must be paid for.
2
Understand the effect on possession
The buyer cannot demand delivery of the sold item until they pay for the increase. The seller may detain the item until payment is made.
The seller has a right of detention (حبس).
3
Consider scenarios of claim and return
If the sold item is claimed by a third party (استحقاق), the buyer can reclaim the full price including the increase. Similarly, if the item is returned due to defect, option of stipulation, or option of inspection, the buyer recovers the entire price paid.
The claim attaches to the whole contract.
4
Apply to agency discount case
From the fatwa of Qadikhan: if an agent sells a house and then discounts part of the price, the discount is valid but does not affect the original contract. The agent must compensate the principal, and the pre-emptor takes the original price.
The agent's discount is not an increase in the sold item.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المرابحة والتولية والحط منه والزيادة في المبيع ويتعلق الاستحقاق بكله وتأجيل كل دين إلا القرض. المدانيات له فائدتين أيضاً قوله : ( ويتعلق الاستحقاق بكله أي بكل ما وقع العقد عليه وبالزيادة فلا يطالب المشتري بالمبيع حتى يدفع الزيادة وللبائع حبسه حتى يقبضها، وإذا استحق المبيع رجع المشتري على بائعه بالكل، وإذا أجار المستحق استحق الكل، وإذا رد المبيع أو خيار شرط أو رؤية رجع المشتري على بائعه بالكل. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان من الشفعة : الوكيل بالبيع إذا باع الدار بألف ثم إن الوكيل أبرأ عن المشتري مائة من الثمن صح حطه ويضمن قدر المحطوط للآمر ويبرأ المشتري عن المائة ويأخذ الشفيع الثمن لأن حط الوكيل لا يلتحق بأصل العقد ا هـ .
Book of Sales, Chapter of Murabaha and Tawliyah: And the discount from it and the increase in the sold item, and the claim attaches to the whole, and the deferment of every debt except the loan. The... also have two benefits. His saying: (And the claim attaches to the whole) meaning to everything on which the contract was concluded and to the increase, so the buyer cannot demand the sold item until he pays the increase, and the seller may detain it until he receives it. And if the sold item is claimed, the buyer takes recourse against his seller for the whole. And if the claimant takes it on lease, he claims the whole. And if he returns the sold item due to a defect or option of stipulation or option of inspection, the buyer takes recourse against his seller for the whole. And in the Fatwas of Qadikhan from the chapter of Shuf'a: If the agent for sale sold a house for a thousand, and then the agent released the buyer from a hundred of the price, his discount is valid, and he guarantees the amount of the discount to the principal, and the buyer is free from the hundred, and the pre-emptor takes the [whole] price, because the agent's discount is not attached to the original contract.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling on the increase in the sold item (الزيادة في المبيع). The author clarifies that the claim (الاستحقاق) attaches to the entire contract, including any increase. This means that if the seller adds something to the sold item after the contract (e.g., a separate asset), it becomes part of the contract, and the buyer cannot take possession of the sold item without paying for the increase as well. The seller may detain the item until the increase is paid. If the item is claimed by a third party (i.e., it turns out not to belong to the seller), the buyer can demand the full price back from his seller, including the increase. Similarly, if the party with a right takes the item on lease, he takes the whole. If the buyer returns the item due to a defect, option of stipulation, or option of inspection, he can reclaim the full price paid. The passage then quotes a fatwa from Qadikhan about an agent: if an agent sells a house and then discounts part of the price to the buyer, the discount is valid, but the agent must compensate the principal for the discounted amount, and the pre-emptor (شفيع) takes the original price, because the agent's discount does not affect the original contract.

Key Terms
زيادة في المبيع (ziyada fi al-mabi'): An addition to the sold item after the contract, considered part of the sale.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Claim or right of a third party to the sold item, affecting the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a seller adds an extra item to the sold item after the contract, what is the ruling?
A) The increase is invalid and the contract stands without it.
B) The buyer must pay for the increase and cannot take the sold item until he does.
C) The buyer may take the sold item and pay for the increase later.
D) The contract is void due to uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
An increase in the sold item after the contract attaches to the whole, so the buyer must pay for it before taking possession, and the seller may detain the item.

Deferment of Debt: Permissible for All Except Loans
Explains that deferment of debt is valid for all debts except loans, and provides a legal trick for loan deferment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferment of debt, distinguish between loans and other debts, and evaluate the legal trick for loan deferment.

Core Idea
Deferment of debt is valid and binding for all debts except loans, as loan deferment would entail riba.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on postponing a debt (ta'jil al-dayn). While creditors may generally defer the payment date of any debt, loans (qard) are treated differently because they are initially benevolent contracts. We will explore the reasoning behind this exception and a controversial legal stratagem that attempts to circumvent it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State the rule: deferment of every debt except a loan is valid (sahih). Note that this includes the price of a sold item or any other debt.
The source says 'صح' meaning legally valid and binding upon mutual agreement.
2
Understand the rationale for the loan exception
A loan (qard) is initially a form of charity (gift). Deferment would transform it into a sale of money on credit, which is riba. Therefore, deferment of a loan is not binding (ghayr lazim).
The reasoning combines two perspectives: the beginning (gift) and the end (exchange).
3
Note the condition of debtor's acceptance
For deferment to be binding, the debtor must accept. If the debtor refuses, the debt remains due immediately.
This highlights that deferment is a mutual modification of the contract, not a unilateral right.
4
Examine the legal trick for loan deferment
The trick involves a surety (kafala): the borrower assigns a surety for the debt with a term. The lender then defers the surety. However, this trick is weak; only al-Hasiri supported it, and it is not relied upon for fatwa.
Abu Yusuf's transmission in al-Siraj seems to allow it, but later scholars reject it as contradicting established principles.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling for fatwa: deferment of loans is not binding; the legal trick is not accepted. One must avoid any arrangement that could lead to riba.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin, with al-Nahr and others confirming the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتأجيل كل دين إلا القرض) أي صح لأن الدين حقه فله أن يؤخره، سواء كان ثمن مبيع أو غيره تيسيراً على من عليه ألا ترى أنه يملك ابراءه مطلقاً فكذا مؤقتاً. ولا بد من قبوله ممن عليه الدين فلو لم يقبله بطلب التأخير فيكون حالاً؛ كذا ذكره الأسبيجابي . ويصح تعليق التأجيل بالشرط فلو قال رب الدين لمن عليه ألف حالة إن دفعت إلي غداً خمسمائة فالخمسمائة الأخرى مؤخرة عنك إلى سنة فهو جائز ؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وإنما لا يؤجل القرض لكونه إعارة وصلة في الابتداء حتى يصح بلفظ الإعارة ولا يملكه يملك التبرع كالصبي والوصي ومعاوضة في الانتهاء فعلى اعتبار الابتداء لا يلزم التأجيل فيه كما في الإعارة إذ لا جبر في التبرع، وعلى اعتبار الانتهاء لا لأنه يصح يصير بيع الدراهم بالدراهم نسيئة وهو ربا، ومرادهم من الصحة اللزوم ومن عدم صحته في القرض عدم اللزوم. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا أجله بعد الاستهلاك أو قبله هو الصحيح، وليس من تأجيل القرض تأجيل بدل الدراهم أو الدنانير المستهلكة إذا باستهلاكها لا تصير قرضاً، والحيلة في لزوم تأجيل القرض أن يحيل المستقرض المقرض على آخر بدينه فيؤجل المقرض ذلك الرجل الثمن التعليق فإذا أبرأته براءة إسقاط وقع ورجع عليها ؛ كذا في الأشباه قوله : (فلا يطالب المشتري بالمبيع الخ) أي لا يكون للمشتري أن يطالب البائع بالمبيع حتى يدفع المشتري له الزيادة وللبائع حبس المبيع حتى يقبضها من المشتري هذا معنى هذه العبارة ولا يخفي أن المراد بالزيادة فيها الزيادة في وقد تقدم ذلك والكلام الآن في الزيادة في المبيع. قوله : (وهي حيلة تأجيل القرض) قال في النهر : لكن في السراج قال أبو يوسف : إذا أقرض رجل رجلاً مالاً فكفل به رجل عنه إلى وقت كان على. الكفيل إلى وقته وعلى المستقرض حالاً اهـ. وسيأتي في كتاب الكفالة ذكر المسألة أيضاً. ونقل المؤلف هناك عن التتارخانية معزياً إلى الذخيرة والغياثية ما يوافق ما في السراج، وذكر في أنفع الوسائل مثله عن عدة كتب وذكر أن هذه الحيلة لم يقل بها أحد غير الحصيري في التحرير وأنه إذا تعارض كلامه وحده مع كلام كل الأصحاب لا يفتي به . قوله : (بل كذلك لا . يصح تأجيل الدين في صورة الخ) قال في النهر بعد ذكره لها : وظاهر كلامهم يعطي أن في هذه المسائل لا يصح التأجيل أصلاً لا أنه
His saying: (And the deferment of every debt except the loan) i.e., it is valid because the debt is his right, so he may defer it, whether it is the price of a sold item or other, as a facility for the debtor. Do you not see that he has the right to release it absolutely, so likewise temporarily. But acceptance from the debtor is necessary; if he does not accept the request for deferment, it remains due immediately. Thus mentioned al-Asbijabi. And deferment may be attached to a condition; so if the creditor says to the debtor who owes a thousand due: 'If you pay me five hundred tomorrow, then the other five hundred are deferred by a year,' it is permissible. Thus in al-Dhakhira. And the loan is not deferred because it is a loan/gift initially, so it is valid by the wording of 'ariyya (gift), and the debtor does not own it but may give charity like a child or guardian, and it is a transaction at the end. So considering the beginning, deferment is not binding, as in 'ariyya, because there is no compulsion in charity. Considering the end, it is not valid because it would become a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit, which is riba. And by 'validity' they mean binding; by 'invalidity' in the loan they mean non-binding. And he made it absolute so it includes whether he deferred it after consumption or before; that is correct. And deferment of the substitute of consumed dirhams or dinars is not deferment of a loan because by consumption they do not become a loan. And the legal trick for binding deferment of a loan is that the borrower assigns the lender to another person for his debt, and then the lender defers that person. ... His saying: (Thus the buyer cannot demand the sold item etc.) i.e., the buyer does not have the right to demand the sold item from the seller until the buyer pays the increase, and the seller may detain the sold item until he receives it. This is the meaning of this expression, and it is not hidden that what is meant by increase here is the increase in... and this was mentioned before. Now the discussion is about the increase in the sold item. His saying: (And it is the legal trick for deferment of a loan) Al-Nahr said: But in al-Siraj, Abu Yusuf said: If a man lends money to another, and a third person becomes surety for it for a term, then the surety is liable at the term, and the borrower remains liable immediately. This will be mentioned in the Chapter of Kafala. And the author transmitted from al-Tatarhaniyya citing al-Dhakhira and al-Ghiyathiyya what agrees with al-Siraj. And he mentioned in Anfa' al-Wasa'il similar from several books, and he mentioned that this legal trick was not said by anyone other than al-Hasiri in al-Tahrir, and that if his statement alone opposes the statements of all the companions, fatwa is not given on it. His saying: (Rather, deferment of debt is not valid in the case of...) Al-Nahr said after mentioning it: The apparent meaning of their statements indicates that in these cases, deferment is not valid at all, not that...
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on deferment of debt (تأجيل الدين). The author states that deferment is valid for all debts except loans (القرض). The reasoning is that debt is the creditor's right, so he may postpone it. However, the debtor must accept; otherwise it remains due. Deferment can be conditional. Loans cannot be deferred because a loan is initially like a gift (عارية), and deferment would make it a sale of money for money on credit, which is riba. The 'validity' here means bindingness; the loan deferment is not binding even if done. The passage then presents a legal trick (حيلة) to achieve binding deferment: the borrower assigns the lender to another person for his debt, and then the lender defers that person. However, this trick is weak; only al-Hasiri supported it, and it is not relied upon for fatwa. The passage ends with a note that in some cases, deferment is not valid at all.

Key Terms
تأجيل الدين (ta'jil al-dayn): Postponement of the due date of a debt.
قرض (qard): Loan of fungible items; considered a beneficence initially.
حيلة (hila): Legal stratagem to achieve a permissible result that would otherwise be prohibited or non-binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is deferment of a loan (qard) treated differently from other debts in Hanafi law?
A) Because loans are not considered debts.
B) Because deferment would turn the loan into a sale of currency on credit, which is riba.
C) Because the debtor has no right to defer.
D) Because loans are initially invalid.

Key Takeaway
Deferment of loans is not binding; the legal trick to make it binding is rejected by the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Deferment of Debts: General Rule and the Loan Exception
Commentary on matn ruling about deferment of debts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that any debt other than a loan may be deferred by agreement, and explain the prohibition of deferring loans due to riba.

Core Idea
A loan cannot be deferred because it becomes a credit sale of money, which is riba.

In Hanafi fiqh, a creditor has the right to postpone the collection of a debt, as it is his right. However, this general permission has a critical exception: loans. This lesson explores the rationale, conditions, and application of this rule based on the commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule and Its Scope
The matn states: 'Deferment of every debt except the loan.' Determine what 'debt' includes (e.g., price of sale, other obligations) and what is excluded (the loan contract itself).
Debts like the price of a sold item can be deferred with the debtor's consent.
2
Understand the Rationale for Excluding Loans
Explain why loans cannot be deferred: initially a loan is a gratuitous transfer (like a gift), and deferring it would transform it into a credit sale of money for money (riba al-nasi'ah).
The text compares this to a loan of fungibles; deferment would be a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit.
3
Recognize the Requirement of Debtor Acceptance
The commentary states that deferment requires the debtor's acceptance. If the debtor does not agree, the debt remains immediately due.
This is because the creditor is not forced to defer; it is a bilateral agreement.
4
Note the Validity of Conditional Deferment
The text gives an example: if the creditor says, 'If you pay me 500 now, the remaining 500 is deferred for a year,' this is valid. Understand the permissibility of suspending deferment on a condition.
This is considered a valid conditional agreement.

قوله: (وتأجيل كل دين إلا القرض) أي صح لأن الدين حقه فله أن يؤخره، سواء كان ثمن مبيع أو غيره تيسيراً على من عليه ألا ترى أنه يملك ابراءه مطلقاً فكذا مؤقتاً. ولا بد من قبوله ممن عليه الدين فلو لم يقبله بطلب التأخير فيكون حالاً؛ كذا ذكره الأسبيجابي . ويصح تعليق التأجيل بالشرط فلو قال رب الدين لمن عليه ألف حالة إن دفعت إلي غداً خمسمائة فالخمسمائة الأخرى مؤخرة عنك إلى سنة فهو جائز ؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وإنما لا يؤجل القرض لكونه إعارة وصلة في الابتداء حتى يصح بلفظ الإعارة ولا يملكه يملك التبرع كالصبي والوصي ومعاوضة في الانتهاء فعلى اعتبار الابتداء لا يلزم التأجيل فيه كما في الإعارة إذ لا جبر في التبرع، وعلى اعتبار الانتهاء لا لأنه يصح يصير بيع الدراهم بالدراهم نسيئة وهو ربا، ومرادهم من الصحة اللزوم ومن عدم صحته في القرض عدم اللزوم. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا أجله بعد الاستهلاك أو قبله هو الصحيح، وليس من تأجيل القرض تأجيل بدل الدراهم أو الدنانير المستهلكة إذا باستهلاكها لا تصير قرضاً، والحيلة في لزوم تأجيل القرض أن يحيل المستقرض المقرض على آخر بدينه فيؤجل المقرض ذلك الرجل الثمن التعليق فإذا أبرأته براءة إسقاط وقع ورجع عليها ؛ كذا في الأشباه قوله : (فلا يطالب المشتري بالمبيع الخ) أي لا يكون للمشتري أن يطالب البائع بالمبيع حتى يدفع المشتري له الزيادة وللبائع حبس المبيع حتى يقبضها من المشتري هذا معنى هذه العبارة ولا يخفى أن المراد بالزيادة فيها الزيادة في وقد تقدم ذلك والكلام الآن في الزيادة في المبيع. قوله : (وهي حيلة تأجيل القرض) قال في النهر : لكن في السراج قال أبو يوسف : إذا أقرض رجل رجلاً مالاً فكفل به رجل عنه إلى وقت كان على. الكفيل إلى وقته وعلى المستقرض حالاً اهـ. وسيأتي في كتاب الكفالة ذكر المسألة أيضاً. ونقل المؤلف هناك عن التتارخانية معزياً إلى الذخيرة والغياثية ما يوافق ما في السراج، وذكر في أنفع الوسائل مثله عن عدة كتب وذكر أن هذه الحيلة لم يقل بها أحد غير الحصيري في التحرير وأنه إذا تعارض كلامه وحده مع كلام كل الأصحاب لا يفتي به . قوله : (بل كذلك لا . يصح تأجيل الدين في صورة الخ) قال في النهر بعد ذكره لها : وظاهر كلامهم يعطي أن في هذه المسائل لا يصح التأجيل أصلاً لا أنه يلزم المحال عليه فيلزم حينئذ ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وإذا لزم فإن كان للمحيل على المحال عليه فلا إشكال وإلا أقر المحيل بقدر المحال به للمحال عليه مؤجلاً إليه. أشار في المحيط وفي الظهيرية القبض المجحود يجوز تأجيله. وفي القنية من كتاب المداينات : قضى القاضي بلزوم الأجل في القرض بعد ما ثبت عنده تأجيل القرض معتمداً على قول مالك وابن أبي ليلى يصح ويلزم الأجل. وفي تلخيص الجامع من كتاب الحوالة : لو كفل بالحال مؤجلاً تأخر الأصيل وإن كان قرضاً لأن الدين واحد وهي حيلة تأجيل القرض إذ يثبت ضمناً ما قصداً كبيع الشرب والطريق، ولا يلزم ما أجل بعد الكفالة إذ موضوعها أن يضيف إلى اللازم بالكفالة إلا الدين حتى لو عكس تأخر عن الأصيل أيضا حذ والإبراء ا هـ . ولم يستثن المصنف رحمه الله تعالى من عدم صحة تأجيل القرض شيئاً واستثنى منه في الهداية ما إذا أوصى أن يقرض من ماله ألف درهم فلاناً إلى سنة حيث يلزم من ثلثه أن يقرضوه ولا يطالبوه قبل المدة لأنه وصية بالتبرع بمنزلة الوصية بالخدمة والسكنى فيلزم حقاً للموصي ولا ينحصر في هذه الصورة بل كذلك إذا كان له قرض على إنسان فأوصى أن يؤجل ولزم كما في القنية. وقد كتبنا في الفوائد الفقهية أن المستثنى لا ينحصر في القرض بل كذلك لا يصح تأجيل الدين في صور : الأولى لو مات المديون وحل المال فأجل الدائن لأن الدين في الذمة وفائدة التأجيل أن يتجر فيؤدي الثمن من نماء المال، فإذا من له الأجل تعين المتروك لقضاء الدين فلا يفيد التأجيل؛ كذا في الخلاصة، وظاهره في كل دين . وذكره في القنية في القرض الثانية أجل المشتري الشفيع في الثمن لم يصح كما سيأتي فيها وهو مذكور في القنية . اهـ. سنة صح وأرثه لم يصح مات أنه يصح . عن وفي الخلاصة : بموت البائع لا يبطل الأجل ويبطل بموت المشتري. الثالثة تأجيل ثمن المبيع عند الإقالة لا كما قدمناه القنية. والحاصل أن تأجيل الدين على ثلاثة أوجه : باطل وهو تأجيل بدلي الصرف والسلم وصحيح غير لازم وهو القرض والدين بعد الموت وتأجيل الشفيع وثمن المبيع بعد الإقالة ولازم فيما عدا ذلك. قال قاضيخان في فتاواه : المديون إذا قال برئت من الأجل أو لا حاجة لي في الأجل لهذا الدين لم يكن إبطالاً للأجل، ولو قال أبطلت الأجل أو قال تركته صار حالاً، والمديون إذا قضى الدين قبل حلول الأجل فاستحق المقبوض من القابض أو وجده زيوفاً فرده كان الدين عليه إلى أجله، ولو اشترى من مديونه شيئاً بالدين وقبضه ثم تقايلا البيع لا يعود الأجل، ولو يصح، ولا يلزم كما هو ظاهر ما في البحر إذ جعله ملحقاً بالفرض ثم قال : والحاصل أن تأجيل الديون على ثلاثة أوجه الخ. وقد علمت ما هو الواقع .اهـ قلت الظاهر أن المراد بالباطل هنا ما لا يجوز فعله والمضي وبالصحيح ما يجوز قوله: (وفي الخلاصة وإبطال الأجل الخ) أي إبطال الأجل
He said: 'And deferment of every debt except the loan' i.e., it is valid because the debt is his right, so he may delay it, whether it is the price of a sold item or otherwise, to make it easier for the debtor. Do you not see that he may discharge it absolutely, so likewise temporarily. Acceptance from the debtor is necessary; if he does not accept the request for deferment, it remains due immediately. Thus mentioned al-Asbijabi. It is valid to suspend the deferment on a condition: if the creditor says to one who owes him a thousand as a spot debt: 'If you pay me five hundred tomorrow, the other five hundred is deferred for you for a year,' it is permissible. Thus in al-Dhakhira. The loan is not deferred because it is a loan and a connection initially, so it is valid with the wording of a loan, and the creditor does not own the right to charity like a minor or executor, and it becomes an exchange at the end. So considering the beginning, deferment is not binding in it, as in a loan, since there is no compulsion in charity; and considering the end, it is not because it would become a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit, which is riba. Their intention of validity is binding, and of its invalidity in the loan is non-binding. He applied it generally, so it includes whether he deferred it after consumption or before—that is the correct view. Deferment of the loan does not include deferment of the substitute for consumed dirhams or dinars because their consumption does not make it a loan. The trick for making deferment of a loan binding is that the borrower transfers the creditor to another person for his debt, and the creditor defers that person. ... He said: 'This is the trick for deferring a loan.' He said in al-Nahr: But in al-Siraj, Abu Yusuf said: If a man lends another money, and a third person becomes a guarantor for him for a term, the guarantor is responsible for the term, and the borrower is immediately liable. This will be mentioned later in the book of Kafala. The author there quotes from al-Tatar Khaniyya attributing to al-Dhakhira and al-Ghiyathiyya what agrees with al-Siraj, and mentions in Anfa' al-Wasa'il similar from several books, and mentions that this trick was not said by anyone except al-Husari in al-Tahrir, and that when his statement alone conflicts with the statements of all the companions, it is not to be issued as a fatwa. He said: 'But likewise, deferment of the debt is not valid in the following case...' He said in al-Nahr after mentioning it: The apparent meaning of their statements is that in these cases deferment is not valid at all, not that it becomes binding on the transferee... If it becomes binding, then if the transferor has a claim on the transferee, there is no problem; otherwise, the transferor acknowledges the amount transferred to the transferee as deferred. He indicated in al-Muhit and al-Zahiriyya that the denied payment may be deferred. In al-Qunyah from the book of Mudayanat: The judge ruled for the binding of the term in the loan after it was established that the deferment of the loan was agreed upon, relying on the statement of Malik and Ibn Abi Layla that it is valid and binding. In Talkhis al-Jami' from the book of Hawala: If someone guarantees a spot debt as deferred, the principal is delayed even if it is a loan, because the debt is one, and this is a trick for deferring the loan, as what is intended indirectly is established, like the sale of irrigation rights and right of way. And what is deferred after guarantee is not binding... He did not exclude anything from the invalidity of deferring a loan. Al-Hidayah excluded the case where one bequeaths that a thousand dirhams be lent to so-and-so for a year; then it becomes binding from his third that they lend it and do not demand it before the term, because it is a bequest of charity, like the bequest of service and dwelling, so it becomes a right of the testator. This is not limited to this case, but likewise if he had a loan on someone and bequeathed that it be deferred, it becomes binding, as in al-Qunyah. We have written in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya that the excluded cases are not limited to the loan, but likewise deferment of the debt is not valid in the following cases: First, if the debtor dies and the debt becomes due, and the creditor defers it, because the debt is in the liability, and the benefit of deferment is for the debtor to trade and pay from the produce of the wealth, so when the deceased (the one with the term) dies, the estate is assigned to pay the debt, so deferment is not beneficial. Thus in al-Khulasa, and it is apparent that it applies to every debt. Al-Qunyah mentioned it regarding the loan. Second, if the buyer defers the preemptor in the price, it is not valid, as will come later. This is mentioned in al-Qunyah. ... In al-Khulasa: With the death of the seller, the term does not become void, but it becomes void with the death of the buyer. Third, deferment of the price of the sold item upon rescission, it is not valid, as we have previously mentioned in al-Qunyah. The summary is that deferment of debts is of three types: invalid—which is deferment of the countervalues in currency exchange and salam; valid but not binding—which is the loan and the debt after death, and the deferment of the preemptor and the price after rescission; and binding in all other cases. Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: If the debtor says 'I am free from the term' or 'I have no need for the term for this debt,' that does not nullify the term. If he says 'I have nullified the term' or 'I have abandoned it,' it becomes due immediately. If the debtor pays the debt before the term, and then the payment is reclaimed from the recipient, or he finds it counterfeit and returns it, the debt remains until its term. If he buys something from his debtor with the debt and takes possession, then they rescind the sale, the term does not return. ... He said: The summary is that deferment of debts is of three types... I said: It appears that by 'invalid' here they mean what is not permissible to do and proceed with, and by 'valid' what is permissible. He said: '(And in al-Khulasa, nullification of the term...)' i.e., nullification of the term.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn statement 'And deferment of every debt except the loan.' The commentator explains that a creditor may defer any debt by agreement with the debtor, including the price of a sale or other debts, but a loan (qard) cannot be deferred because it is a gratuitous contract initially (like a loan) and if deferred it would become a sale of money for money on credit, which is riba. However, there is debate about certain exceptions: if the debtor dies and the creditor defers the debt from the estate, it is not valid. Also, there is discussion of a legal trick (hila) to make deferment binding by using a guarantor or transfer, but this is not accepted by most scholars except al-Husari. The passage concludes by categorizing all deferments into three types: invalid (for currency exchange and salam), valid but not binding (loan and debt after death, and certain cases), and binding (all other cases).

Key Terms
تأجيل الدين (ta'jīl al-dayn): Postponing the payment of a debt to a future date by agreement between creditor and debtor.
القرض (al-qarḍ): A loan of fungible goods or money to be repaid in kind, which is a gratuitous contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is deferment of a loan (qard) not valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because a loan is considered a charity, and charity cannot be deferred.
B) Because it would cause hardship to the debtor.
C) Because it would turn into a sale of money on credit, which is riba.
D) Because the creditor must always demand immediate repayment.

Key Takeaway
Deferment of any debt other than a loan is valid and binding with mutual consent; loans are excluded because deferment leads to riba.
